Biden-led blue wave and progress on COVID-19 vaccine","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/dollar-biden-blue-wave-covid-vaccine-goldman-sachs-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8406b2642e9400180b5479?format=jpeg\" alt=\"joe biden\" height=\"1443\" width=\"2886\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Investors should sell the dollar, as the chances grow for a clear win by Democrat candidate Joe Biden in the November presidential election and for the development of a successful COVID-19 vaccine, Goldman Sachs said in a note on Friday.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>Strategists led by Zach Pandl said: \"Although there are uncertainties around both, the risks are skewed toward dollar weakness, and we see relatively low odds of the most dollar-positive outcome—a win by Mr Trump, combined with a meaningful vaccine delay.\"</strong></li><li><strong>Goldman said these two events could prompt the dollar to fall to its 2018 lows.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>The bank recommends selling the dollar against a currency basket made up of the South African rand, Indian rupee and the Mexican peso and advises buying the Australian and Canadian dollars and the euro.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>Investors should sell the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/us-dollar-index\">dollar</a>, as chances grow for a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-outlook-biden-blue-wave-boost-growth-goldman-sachs-2020-10-1029649255#\">decisive win</a> by Democrat Joe Biden at next month's election and as progress continues towards an effective vaccine against COVID-19, Goldman Sachs strategists said on Friday.</p><p>Strategists led by Zach Pandl said in a note the two key drivers for the currencies are now the Democrats taking control of both Congress and the Senate in a Biden win on November 3 and progress on a vaccine.</p><p>\"Although there are uncertainties around both, the risks are skewed toward dollar weakness, and we see relatively low odds of the most dollar-positive outcome—a win by Mr. Trump combined with a meaningful vaccine delay,\" Goldman said.</p><p>Goldman said the chances of a so-called \"blue wave\" have risen to more than 60%, based on Biden's growing lead over President Donald Trump in the polls.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-companies-with-best-profit-growth-goldman-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GOLDMAN SACHS: Buy these 15 stocks set to deliver the strongest possible profit growth and subsequent returns through year-end</a></em></p><p>\"In our view, a \"blue wave\" US election and favorable news on the vaccine timeline could return the trade-weighted dollar and dollar index to their 2018 lows,\" the bank said.&#160;</p><p>The US dollar index, which tracks the strength of the greenback against six other major currencies, has dropped around 5% in the last six months and is around 5.3% above where it traded in January 2018.</p><p>Goldman suggests investors should short the dollar against a volatility-weighted basket made up of the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/usd-zar\">South African rand</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/usd-inr\">Indian rupee</a> and the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/usd-mxn\">Mexican peso,</a> as well as buying <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/aud-usd\">Australian</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/usd-cad\">Canadian</a> dollars and the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eur-usd\">euro</a>.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-expert-foresees-drop-massive-financial-crisis-bankruptcies-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">'The largest financial crisis in history': A 47-year market vet says the COVID-19 crash was merely a 'fake-out sell-off' — and warns of an 80% stock plunge fraught with bank failures and bankruptcies</a></em></p><p>\"The wide margin in current polls reduces the risk of a delayed election result, and the prospect for near-term vaccine breakthroughs may provide a backstop for risky assets,\" Goldman said.</p><p>Moderna and Pfizer, two front-runners in the race to develop a COVID-19 vaccine, are showing steady signs of progress, Goldman said.&#160;</p><p>Moderna has indicated its first interim analysis of its phase 3 trial should be available by November and the company's CEO, Stéphane Bancel, told the Financial Times earlier this month its vaccine is likely to be ready for use in late March, or early April 2021.&#160;</p><p>Meanwhile, Pfizer said the company expects to have a \"conclusive readout\" on the efficacy of its vaccine trial by the end of October.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-amazon-prime-day-retail-investing-strategy-proshares-hyman-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" Sardana)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f8406b2642e9400180b5479?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn86@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-240_54d983147664dd1b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fWPgte7Z_JE:tYJLKeMC2Zw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn63@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-05-03-168_7624942ebc18a167.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fWPgte7Z_JE:tYJLKeMC2Zw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn49@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-53-874_de9f115eb620cfb6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fWPgte7Z_JE:tYJLKeMC2Zw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn79@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-00-812_f4715e189eaf9714.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/fWPgte7Z_JE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn99@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-52-827_1ecdb6d36ebd9c26.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289884},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"Trump will be slammed with a pile of personal lawsuits once he leaves office. Here are 9 major ones he'll have to face.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/lawsuits-trump-will-face-when-he-leaves-office-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f61857057b7da001ee11e02?format=jpeg\" alt=\"President Donald Trump\" height=\"750\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump&#39;s healthcare agenda includes lowering prescription drug prices and tackling surprise medical bills.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mandel Ngan/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>While in office, President Donald Trump has largely evaded the civil suits against him.</li>\n<li>That could change once the president leaves office, which would be in January if he loses the election against former Vice President Joe Biden.</li>\n<li>Legal experts <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-campaign-investigation-probe-doj-justice-fec-mueller-election-2020-8\">who spoke to Business Insider</a> previously said they believed Trump may face a number of legal headaches if he is voted out of office.</li>\n<li>There are at least 9 major ongoing lawsuits that involve the president, ranging from defamation cases resulting from his sexual assault denials to allegations he and his children misled victims to sell goods for a multi-level marketing company.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Before and during his presidency, Donald Trump has been sued dozens of times. The lawsuits have alleged everything from business deals gone wrong to sexual assault.</p><p>Some cases have been resolved or dismissed. But a number of them remain active, suspended or slowed until he leaves office. He he will have to face the onslaught of lawsuits if he loses reelection and becomes a private citizen once again.</p><p>As Business Insider's Dave Levinthal previously reported, Trump will likely face <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-campaign-investigation-probe-doj-justice-fec-mueller-election-2020-8\">a litany of federal investigations</a> if he loses to former Vice President Joe Biden next month. He <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/07/18/justice-department-weighed-rule-not-charging-president-ending-trump-hush-money-case/1769339001/\">may also be indicted for his role in covering up hush-money payments to Karen McDougal</a> — a plot that sent his former lawyer Michael Cohen to prison.</p><p>Norm Eisen, a senior fellow in Governance Studies at the Brookings Institution, told Business Insider&#160;there were several reasons Trump has been successful in avoiding court appearances.</p><p>\"Part of it is the power of the presidency,\" he said. \"Part of it is the slowness of the system. He is the target of a number of litigation matters and investigations, but he's been able to take advantage, for example <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trumps-business-and-tax-records-likely-wont-be-public-before-the-2020-election-2020-7\">in the Vance [tax record] case</a>, of the extreme slowness of the system.\"</p><p>Some legal actions taken against Trump and his web of organizations have been successful. He, along with his children, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/all-the-investigations-lawsuits-involving-president-donald-trump-businesses-2018-12#the-lawsuits-and-investigations-involving-the-trump-organization-and-trump-foundation-5\">agreed to dissolve the Donald J. Trump Foundation</a> after a New York state investigation found they repeatedly lied about charity work.</p><p>Some have been settled in arbitration, like the 2018 lawsuit from Noel Cintron, Trump's longtime driver, who <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-08-30/trump-s-personal-driver-drops-lawsuit-over-unpaid-overtime\">alleged he was owed $200,000 in unpaid overtime</a>. Other plaintiffs, like Alva Johnson, who alleged Trump kissed her without consent at a 2016 Florida rally, have dropped their lawsuits. \"I'm fighting against a person with unlimited resources,\" <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/alva-johnson-drops-lawsuit-against-president-trump-im-fighting-against-a-person-with-unlimited-resources-6?ref=scroll\">she told the Daily Beast after dropping the case in 2019</a>.</p><p>\"There's going to be an accumulating number of these legal actions that are going to squeeze him more and more,\" Eisen said. \"It will be more intense if he's not in the office and does not have the excuses of the presidency to block things. But in any event, he's facing accountability.\"&#160;</p><p>Here are nine of the ongoing lawsuits Trump still has to deal with.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tTrump faces a defamation lawsuit from \"The Apprentice\" contestant Summer Zervos.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f749c990ab50d00184ad428?format=jpeg\" alt=\"summer zervos\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In this Oct. 18, 2018, file photo, Summer Zervos leaves New York state appellate court in New York.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Associated Press/Mary Altaffer</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Summer Zervos, a contestant during the 2005 season of Trump's reality show \"The Apprentice\" sued President Trump in 2017, claiming that the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gloria-allred-summer-zervos-trump-2017-1\">president defamed her when denying her allegations</a> that he sexually assaulted her in 2007.</p><p>In 2019, Zervos <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/604ae995404f4421a113d327b1be86a4\">claimed she had evidence</a>, including calendar entries and emails, to back up her claims.</p><p>Trump was at one point given a deadline to provide a deposition before the end of January 2020, but the case <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/01/07/politics/summer-zervos-trump-lawsuit/index.html\">has since been paused</a>.</p>\n\tThe Washington, DC, attorney general sued Trump Organization, claiming it was knowingly overcharged for services at the president's DC hotel.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7235980ab50d00184acd8c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO: A general view of the Trump International Hotel seen in Washington, U.S., April 18, 2019. REUTERS/Amr Alfiky\" height=\"1998\" width=\"2664\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A general view of the Trump International Hotel seen in Washington.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In September, a federal judge in Washington, DC, denied Trump's request to dismiss the lawsuit, which alleges that the Trump Organization improperly used nonprofit funds to enrich Trump's businesses, as <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/lawsuit-against-trump-inaugural-committee-can-continue-judge-rules-n1239703\">NBC News</a> reported.&#160;</p><p>The suit was brought in January by Washington, DC, Attorney General Karl Racine over claims that Trump's inaugural committee spent more than $1 million at the president's DC hotel despite the fact it knew it was being overcharged for services, according to the report.</p>\n\tAdvice columnist E. Jean Carroll has also sued Trump, alleging he defamed her in denying that he raped her in the 90s.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f74ac020ab50d00184ad4b8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"E. Jean Carroll\" height=\"1400\" width=\"1866\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>E. Jean Carroll accused President Donald Trump of raping her in a New York department store in the mid-90s.</p><p>Following the president's denial of the allegations, Caroll in November 2019 <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/e-jean-carroll-files-defamation-lawsuit-against-donald-trump-2019-11\">sued the president for defamation</a>.&#160;</p><p>In a largely atypical move in September 2020, the White House <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/white-house-asked-justice-department-defend-trump-carroll-defamation-lawsuit-2020-9\">asked the Department of Justice to intervene in defending the</a> president in the defamation suit.</p>\n\tThe president still faces a lawsuit stemming from a 2015 altercation between his security and a group of protesters.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f74aef70ab50d00184ad4cd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump tower\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A guard stands outside of Trump Tower on Fifth Avenue in Manhattan on August 24, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a Platt/Getty</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<section><p>The lawsuit was brought by a group of Mexican-Americans who protested at a 2015 rally outside of Trump Tower in New York.</p><p>The plaintiffs claim security guards shoved them, destroyed their signs, and that Trump's head of security punched one of them in the head while another attempted to choke a protester, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/09/25/judge-stays-order-trump-testify-about-fight-between-his-security-guards-protesters/\">The Washington Post</a> previously reported.</p></section><p>In September 2019, a federal judge ordered Trump to testify in the case, although another judge issued a temporary stay against the order, according to the Post.</p>\n\tThe New York attorney general is also suing the Trump Organization to compel it to comply with her investigation.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f74af6c74fe5b0018a8e3f7?format=jpeg\" New York.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kathy Willens/Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In August, New York Attorney General Letitia James brought a lawsuit against the Trump Organization in a state court in Manhattan, as part of an attempt to enforce an investigatory subpoena against the president's son, Eric, and his personal attorney, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-08-24/new-york-sues-trump-organization-erik-trump-court-filing-shows\">according to Bloomberg</a>.</p><p>In an August 21 letter, the attorney generals office said it \"has not concluded its investigation and has not reached any determination regarding whether the facts identified to date establish violations of any applicable laws.\"</p><p><a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/09/03/judge-orders-trump-company-to-court-for-new-york-subpoenas.html\">As CNBC</a> noted, James is investigating whether the Trump Organization inaccurately valued real estate on financial statements in order to obtain loans and economic and tax benefits.</p>\n\tThe president's former personal lawyer has sued the Trump Organization for nearly $2 million in unpaid fees.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f444d4b42f43f001ddfec6d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO: Michael Cohen, U.S. President Donald Trump&#39;s former lawyer, victims into selling products for American Communications Network.</p><p>The group claims the Trump family misled them in order to enrich themselves from the multi-level marketing company, which charged people $499 to sell the goods, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-marketing-lawsuit/trump-family-loses-bid-to-move-marketing-scam-lawsuit-to-arbitration-idUSKCN21R2OH\">according to Reuters</a>.&#160;</p>\n\tThe president's niece is suing Trump and his siblings.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f74c05d0ab50d00184ad53d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mary trump donald trump 2\" height=\"1500\" href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-calls-niece-who-wrote-book-unstable-rightfully-shunned-2020-8\">in July published a book criticizing him</a>, has sued the president, his sister, Mary, and his late brother Robert for cheating her out of an inheritance.</p><p>In the lawsuit, filed in a New York state court in September, she <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mary-trump-sues-the-president-and-family-for-fraud-2020-9\">accused the family of fraud</a> and of a scheme \"to siphon funds away from her interests, conceal their grift, and deceive her about the true value of what she had inherited.\"</p>\n\tTrump Hotels is being sued for its actions relating to a property it formerly managed in Panama.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f74c7f474fe5b0018a8e49c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trump hotel panama\" height=\"2388\" width=\"3184\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>View of the hotel the initial suit, Orestes Fintiklis and his fund Ithaca Capital Investments, which took control of the property from Trump International Hotels Management in 2018, claimed that Trump mismanaged the Panama hotel. They requested $15 million in damages, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-03-30/trump-must-defend-fraud-claims-over-panama-hotel\">as Bloomberg reported</a>.</p><p>Fintiklis also claimed he and his fund faced millions of dollars in liabilities because Trump underpaid taxes on the project. In March 2020, a federal judge allowed Trump's former business partners to amend their suit to add claims of fraud and breach of contract, according to the report.</p>\n</div><div Dietsch/REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Sen. Amy Klobuchar called the Senate's Supreme Court nomination hearings a \"sham\" and urged Americans to call their senators and voice their opposition during her opening statement on Monday.&#160;&#160;</li>\n<li>Klobuchar said Judge Amy Coney Barrett will be quickly confirmed along partisan lines unless voters protest President Donald Trump's third Supreme Court nominee by petitioning their representatives.</li>\n<li>\"This isn't Donald Trump's country, it is yours,\" Klobuchar said. \"This shouldn't be Donald Trump's judge, it should be yours.\"&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Sen. Amy Klobuchar, a Minnesota Democrat, called the Senate's Supreme Court nomination hearings a \"sham\" and urged Americans to call their senators and voice their opposition during her opening statement on Monday.&#160;&#160;</p><p>\"We cannot divorce this nominee and her views from the election we are in,\" Klobuchar said on the first day of four days of confirmation hearings for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-to-pick-judge-amy-coney-barrett-to-replace-ginsburg-on-the-supreme-court-2020-9\">Judge Amy Coney Barrett</a>.&#160;</p><p>Klobuchar, a former presidential candidate, argued that Barrett will be quickly confirmed along partisan lines unless voters protest President Donald Trump's third Supreme Court nominee by petitioning their representatives.</p><p>\"This hearing is a sham. I think it shows real messed up priorities from the Republican Party,\" Klobuchar said. \"But I am here to do my job, to tell the truth. To all Americans, we don't have some clever procedural way to stop this sham. To stop them from rushing through a nominee.\"</p><p>She went on, \"Let me tell you a political secret: I doubt that it will be a brilliant cross-examination that's going to change this judge's trajectory this week. No, it is you. It is you calling Republican senators and telling them enough is enough ... It is you voting even when they try to do everything to stop you. It is you making your own blueprint for the future, instead of crying defeat.\"&#160;</p><p>Like all her fellow Democrats on the committee, Klobuchar argued that Barrett's stated opposition to the Supreme Court's 2012 ruling upholding the Affordable Care Act puts tens of millions of Americans at risk of losing their health insurance and other protections. The senator told the story of a constituent with diabetes who'd lose protections for her preexisting condition if Obamacare were overturned — a case the Supreme Court is scheduled to hear shortly after the election.&#160;</p><p>The senator ended her statement by speaking directly to American voters.&#160;</p><p>\"This isn't Donald Trump's country, it is yours,\" Klobuchar said. \"This shouldn't be Donald Trump's judge, it should be yours.\"&#160;</p><p>Senators on the Judiciary Committee each have 10 minutes to deliver their opening statements on Monday. Barrett's questioning will begin on Tuesday.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;CBS News  (@CBSNews) <a company's driver-assistance technology that can steer, accelerate, and brake automatically. The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-will-hike-price-semi-autonomous-full-self-driving-package-2020-4\">Full Self-Driving package</a>, an $8,000 option, includes features that allow cars to change lanes, recognize stop signs and traffic lights, and park automatically, but the add-on is far from fully autonomous, despite its name.&#160;</p><p>At Tesla's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-battery-day-announcements-highlights-elon-musk-annual-shareholder-meeting-2020-9\">\"Battery Day\" event</a> last month, Musk announced that the company had overhauled the Autopilot code base and hinted that a new and improved beta version would be released shortly.&#160;</p><p>\"I think we'll hopefully release a private beta of Autopilot — the full self-driving version of Autopilot in, I think, a month or so, and then people will really understand just the magnitude of the change,\" Musk said. \"It's profound.\"</p><p>Although Tesla has steadily added capabilities to the Full Self-Driving package, Musk has repeatedly missed aggressive goals for the introduction of fully autonomous tech, which no carmaker currently offers.</p><p>In 2016, the CEO <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-autonomous-tesla-drive-across-country-by-end-of-2017-2016-10\">said</a> a Tesla would be able to drive itself across the US by the end of the following year. think.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>\"</strong><strong>We're seeing behaviors by companies and consumers that are just not consistent with the national narrative that this economy is hanging by a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/video/2020/10/12/leutholds-paulsen-markets-show-signs-of-consumer-small-business-confidence.html\">told CNBC on Monday</a> that the economy is not as weak as many believe, and highlighted multiple data points that he said indicate a strong recovery is underway.&#160;</p><p>\"To me the financial markets and the corporate and individual behaviors tell a very different narrative than I hear about every day,\" the chief investment strategist said on Monday.&#160;</p><p>He pointed to the recent stock rally that's been led by cyclical and small-cap stocks. These stocks are sensitive to an economic recovery and their gains are a good sign, Paulsen said. He also cited rising commodity prices and increased initial-public-offering activity as bullish signals.&#160;</p><p>The chief strategist added: \"We're seeing behaviors by companies and consumers that are just not consistent with the national narrative that this economy is hanging by a thread and consumers and businesses are petrified in fear.\"</p><p>Housing, auto, and durable goods sales have been rising, he said, adding that these are purchases that are made by consumers who feel confident and secure financially.</p><p>On the job front, he said that temporary jobs as a percentage of total jobs are rising every month, and that's a precursor to \"better job creation down the road.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-amazon-prime-day-retail-investing-strategy-proshares-hyman-2020-10\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"\">The global investment strategist at a $44 billion ETF shop explains why the pandemic-fueled boom of online retail is set to accelerate — and shares 5 stocks to watch other than Amazon ahead of its Prime Day</a></em></p><p>Companies' capital goods orders are at the highest level since 2018, and \"those are investments into the future — you only do that if you're optimistic,\" Paulsen said.&#160;</p><p>The strategist also said the economy may have not seen the full benefits from the first stimulus because historically fiscal policies take about a year to help the economy.<br><br>\"We could have a surprisingly solid, healthy, maybe even accelerating economic growth over the coming quarters because of what we did six, nine, 12 months ago, and I don't think that gets enough attention,\" he said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Emily Graffeo)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f7dec0e94fce90018f7ba79?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn77@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-234_1c901c503989655e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=e62pdXs3hVU:ia2rG2eOd_s:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn27@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-685_f83b15779e94f0a5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=e62pdXs3hVU:ia2rG2eOd_s:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn53@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-54-333_5b10c76bd017f83b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=e62pdXs3hVU:ia2rG2eOd_s:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn47@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-59-816_7d85a6b1707fc365.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/e62pdXs3hVU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn5@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-55-644_9551f46933f6d464.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289790},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"An app that allowed people in China to skirt the nation's internet ban to use Facebook and Google launched last week — then it disappeared","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-google-chinese-firewall-app-tuber-down-qihoo-360-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8474c3642e9400180b5575?format=jpeg\" alt=\"twitter iphone china\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Beata Zawrzel/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>An app that allows people in China to use Facebook, Google, and other foreign platforms &#8212; which are blocked in the Communist nation &#8212; has disappeared from app stores, according to CNBC.</li>\n<li>The Tuber app, backed by a subsidiary of China-based Qihoo 360, launched last week, including on Apple and Huawei's app stores. It is now reportedly unavailable on both.</li>\n<li>China has a track record of censoring the internet for its citizens, restricting the kind of content they are able to access through websites and other services.</li>\n<li>Internet users in China have been able to skirt the nation's \"Great Firewall\" of banned websites by using virtual private networks, or VPNs.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>An app designed to allow people in China to use Facebook, Google, Twitter, and other foreign platforms— which are blocked by the government — has disappeared from app stores shortly after launching, <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/10/12/chinese-app-that-let-users-access-google-facebook-has-disappeared.html\">CNBC reported Monday</a>.</p><p>The Tuber app allows online Chinese users to skirt the nation's \"Great Firewall,\" an internet ban that blocks many popular US apps in the Communist country. The get-around was short-lived — it launched last week, and after a journalist with the state-backed publication Global Times <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RitaBai/status/1314539100343476224\">tweeted</a> about it, Tuber <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RitaBai/status/1314854115382497281\">reportedly</a> disappeared from the Huawei app store. The app, which is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/new-chinese-browser-lets-users-get-around-great-firewall/\">backed by a subsidiary</a> of the Chinese cybersecurity firm Qihoo 360, is also now unavailable on Apple's App Store, according to CNBC. Qihoo 360 did not immediately respond to Business Insider's request for comment.</p><p>China has a long history of censoring the internet, strictly regulating the kinds of websites and services users can access. Its \"Great Firewall\" <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/major-us-tech-companies-blocked-from-operating-in-china-2019-5\">bans a slew of US tech firms</a> from being able to reach millions of users in the Eastern nation, but some have been able to get around it by using virtual private networks, or VPNs.</p><p>The Tuber app allowed residents to access banned websites without the need for VPNs. However, a test of the app from <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/new-chinese-browser-lets-users-get-around-great-firewall/\">TechCrunch</a> revealed it was still somewhat censored, with politically sensitive terms such as \"Tiananmen\" showing no results. The outlet also found that Chinese citizens were required to provide a phone number to use the Tuber app, meaning their identity could be potentially shared with officials.</p><p>News of Tuber's disappearance from app stores comes as tensions continue to grow heated between the US and China. The Trump administration has cracked down on Chinese apps and services, with the president's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/can-trump-ban-tiktok-no-legal-experts-cfius-alternative-options-2020-7\">attempts to ban the popular video-sharing app TikTok</a> — owned by Beijing-based ByteDance — being a prime example. President Trump has also sought to ban the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tencent-explained-wechat-owner-trump-china-executive-order-2020-8\">popular Tencent-owned social app WeChat.&#160;</a></p><p>Federal judges in late September temporarily blocked Trump's attempts to ban both TikTok and&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-judge-blocks-wechat-ban-trump-2020-9\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"dc345e535bbf3ea44e90fc59d0fece57\">WeChat,&#160;</a>but their futures in the US remain uncertain. A hearing is slated for&#160;<a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-tiktok-ban/u-s-judge-to-hold-november-4-hearing-on-commerce-dept-tiktok-ban-idUSKBN26R2KQ\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"9c17d20a1a273670c1cce2f252bf7fb3\">November 4</a>, when a federal judge will decide whether or not to allow the administration to ban transactions with TikTok. TikTok is still in negotiations with Oracle for a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-oracle-partnership-trump-china-bytedance-explainer-2020-9\">potential sale of its US operations</a>, a deal that will need the approval of US regulators.&#160;&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/wl3UT3_mF2U\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Oct 2020 16:20:05 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f8474c3642e9400180b5575?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"4e2aadd51bfbfa5d7d00b5b2444a2732","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn15@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-50-672_a79ca3e70906fd21.webp","destWidth":1777,"destHeight":1333,"sourceBytes":24116,"destBytes":24116,"author":"insider@insider.com (Katie Canales)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f8474c3642e9400180b5575?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn15@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-50-672_a79ca3e70906fd21.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=wl3UT3_mF2U:hxbkShdVfZQ:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn61@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-05-01-347_dcd499e2af94ebd7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=wl3UT3_mF2U:hxbkShdVfZQ:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn41@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-05-00-275_c86b459de34888eb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=wl3UT3_mF2U:hxbkShdVfZQ:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn69@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-54-581_bb17e18f743cd6f4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/wl3UT3_mF2U":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn5@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-03-459_301235639ec5fdc7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289775},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"Google is planning to add new 'hub' offices to provide flexibility for employees, and experts say these networks of satellite offices are the future in Silicon Valley","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-offices-post-coronavirus-hub-spokes-satellite-model-experts-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c3696b2fa21001d8daa0c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Amazon Boulder headquarters offices\" height=\"1730\" width=\"2307\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Amazon&#39;s office in Boulder, Colorado.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Helen H. Richardson/The Denver Post via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The future of the tech office isn't clustered in Silicon Valley, experts told Business Insider.</li>\n<li>Instead, tech companies will likely adopt a \"hub-and-spoke\" model, with satellite offices peppered across the US.</li>\n<li>In a post-coronavirus era, employees may have a \"remote-first\" work schedule, and commute to a satellite office when they need to from wherever they live.&#160;</li>\n<li>Amazon, Apple, and Uber have already started to adopt something similar. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-adds-jobs-new-office-hub-locations-2020-8\">Amazon recently announced</a> a $1.4 billion investment in expanding its offices in six US cities outside of Seattle, while <a href=\"https://www.dallasnews.com/business/technology/2019/08/20/uber-makes-it-official-it-will-set-up-major-hub-in-downtown-dallas-by-end-of-year/\">Uber</a> and <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2019/11/apple-expands-in-austin/\">Apple</a> have each made major expansions in Texas.</li>\n<li>This model allows companies to keep the \"prestige\" of a Bay Area headquarters, but expand their talent pools outside Silicon Valley and save money on labor costs, says one expert.</li>\n<li>This could be good for employees, too: It allows workers to live outside of major cities while still being able to access the perks of an office, like technology or socialization.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>When will it be safe for tech employees to return to the office? What happens to employees who want to leave Silicon Valley? And what does the future of the office look like?&#160;</p><p>These are the questions that major tech companies are grappling with as the coronavirus crisis stretches into the fall. Many large tech firms, including giants like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-extends-work-from-home-june-2021-coronavirus-2020-8\">Facebook</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-employees-working-from-home-summer-2021-report-2020-7\">Google</a>, have pushed back plans to return to the office until summer 2021, and have said they anticipate a rise in remote work.</p><p>But experts told Business Insider that the office — and Silicon Valley — will look <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/going-back-to-work-office-design-coronavirus-2020-5\">very different</a> by then. With workers <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/san-francisco-bay-area-tech-workers-leaving-remote-survey-2020-8\">leaving</a> the Bay Area and companies wary to have thousands of employees all in one place, San Francisco may not be the central tech headquarters it's been for decades.</p><p>Instead, the experts say, tech companies are going to expand outward, with small satellite offices peppered throughout the US.</p><p>\"We're going to start to see satellite locations rather than singular HQs,\" Melissa Hanley, CEO of the Bay Area design firm Blitz, told Business Insider. \"We might say, 'Hey, you don't have to commute two hours. We're going to have a little satellite office with all the resources you need out in the 'burbs.'\"&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3ec8a642f43f001ddfe1ed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Google Boulder Colorado office worker\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Google employee at the company&#39;s office in Colorado.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AAron Ontiveroz/The Denver Post via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>A hub-and-spoke model</h2><p>Adam Segal, the CEO of workplace management technology company Cove, said he expects most companies will start to adopt a \"remote-first approach,\" meaning that working at home is the norm, not the exception. While workers might have worked remotely one or two days per week in pre-coronavirus times, in the future, that will be reversed, Segal said.</p><p>\"So what does that mean? You just have less dedicated desks,\" Segal told Business Insider. \"No one misses their desk — that's not why you go to the office. You miss people, the socialization.\"</p><p>Segal agrees with Hanley that the future of the office will be a so-called \"hub-and-spoke\" model: Companies would have a \"hub,\" or headquarters, in a major city, then have \"spokes\" anywhere in America connected by the same technology system. With Cove's system, for example, you'd be able to look up office locations in your area, see which of your colleagues was working there, and book a desk of your choice for the day.&#160;</p><p>Google is planning on a future that includes office hubs, according to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-ceo-elaborates-future-office-plans-as-employees-demand-answers-2020-10\">leaked audio obtained by Business Insider's Hugh Langley</a>. During an October 1 all-hands meeting, Google CEO Sundar Pichai said the company is planning on adding new, smaller hub offices, which will give employees more flexibility around where they live.&#160;</p><p>\"In the future when we think about it, we do see the majority of Googlers' roles will continue to be tied to a particular office and that they will live within some reasonable distance of that office,\" Pichai said during the all-hands. \"What we are doing is expanding the number of offices we see as hubs so that people will have a lot more choice in their lives.\"</p><p>Pichai also used the phrase \"hybrid-flexible\" to describe how Googlers will work going forward, which could mean that employees will have the option to both work remotely and report to the office.&#160;</p><p>Twitter CEO Jack Dorsey <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jack-dorsey-twitter-san-francisco-office-decentralized-coronavirus-2020-8\">recently hinted at a satellite model</a> for Twitter's workers. Dorsey told \"The Boardroom: Out of Office\" podcast host Rich Kleiman that he's been working on \"decentralizing\" Twitter's workforce, and that many entrepreneurs he talks to aren't interested in a big San Francisco headquarters anymore. \"Here we are, an internet company, that's completely centralizing in San Francisco,\" Dorsey said. \"We're not living up to the ideals of what the internet inspired us to be and what it can show.\"&#160;</p><p>Companies like Amazon are already starting to meet employees where they are. The company recently announced <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-adds-jobs-new-office-hub-locations-2020-8\">a $1.4 billion investment</a> to expand its physical offices in six cities across the US: Dallas, Detroit, Denver, New York, Phoenix, and San Diego. It's also hiring 3,500 new employees, but not at its main headquarters in Seattle — these workers will report into those hubs spread across the US.&#160;</p><p>Tracy Brower, a sociologist and principal in the applied research and consulting group at furniture manufacturer Steelcase, said she's already hearing from clients who are mulling a switch to satellite offices, in part because they would save on real estate costs in major cities.</p><p>But she also sees benefits for employees. For one, satellite offices may be safer; workers wouldn't have to worry about commuting in crowded downtowns or trying to socially distance in the elevator of a high-rise building.&#160;</p><p>There would also be an improvement in quality of life. \"Satellites are really more convenient,\" Brower told Business Insider, arguing that they give workers more choice in how they work. \"I might come to a satellite for great technology that my company offers, and I don't have the same thing at home.\"</p><p>For workers sick of staying at home or feeling creatively stuck without the ability to easily work with others, a satellite office could satisfy some of those feelings, Brower said. \"A lot of times, the reason we want to get together is for new ideas, for new thinking, to be stimulated by the people around us.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c488942f43f001ddfda45?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Cove office tech examples\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2521\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An example of Cove&#39;s software in action.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Cove</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Bay Area vs. anywhere else</h2><p>Satellite offices aren't a new concept. In the era after 9/11, for example, <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB1031706785440337155\">the banking industry</a> went the route of satellite offices, setting up hubs outside of lower Manhattan and New York City.&#160;</p><p>The coronavirus may have just sped up a trend that was already percolating in the tech industry over the last few years.</p><p>John Boyd, a principal at corporate location consultancy The Boyd Company, used Uber as an example. In August 2019, Uber announced plans to <a href=\"https://www.dallasnews.com/business/technology/2019/08/20/uber-makes-it-official-it-will-set-up-major-hub-in-downtown-dallas-by-end-of-year/\">build a new hub for 3,000 employees in the Dallas area</a>. The new office is expected to become Uber's largest outside of the Bay Area.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Similarly, in November 2019, Apple broke ground on <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2019/11/apple-expands-in-austin/\">a brand-new, $1 billion Austin campus</a> that spans 3 million square feet. It's expected to open in 2022 and will house 5,000 employees to start.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3ec7ac42f43f001ddfe1ea?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple Austin satellite office\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Apple&#39;s campus in Austin, Texas.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Anthony Smith/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Boyd says that while companies may keep headquarters in the Bay Area for prestige, lower labor costs also make satellite offices appealing.</p><p>\"Labor costs in Raleigh, North Carolina, or Tampa, Florida, can be 25 to 30% less than in Palo Alto, California,\" Boyd said. Moving 4,000 or 5,000 jobs to these markets can mean millions in savings for tech firms.</p><p>Tech companies, however, would need to make those satellite offices desirable for people who don't already live there — or who want the lifestyle of places like Palo Alto. \"They need to offer the type of lifestyle amenities that Tesla employees in Palo Alto view as favorable or desirable,\" Boyd said.</p><p>Boyd said there wes a slew of cities well-positioned to welcome a tech workforce: Nashville, Raleigh, Tampa, Miami, Austin, Salt Lake City, Las Vegas, and Phoenix.</p><p>One thing all the experts agreed on: The office isn't going away, it's just changing.</p><p>\"I don't think the office is dead, I think that's hyperbole and sort of ridiculous,\" Hanley of Blitz, the design firm, said. \"People need community, people need culture, they need contact, and that will not go away.\"</p><p>&#160;</p><p><em><br></em><em>The Business Insider Global Trends Festival will take place on the 19th-23rd of October. 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"An auto-manufacturing expert says Tesla's days of production hell have put it '10 years ahead' of the competition","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-10-years-ahead-of-competition-manufacturing-expert-sandy-munro-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ea2525ad553f82b204b2306?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO: Tesla China-made Model 3 vehicles are seen during a delivery event at its factory in Shanghai, China January 7, 2020. REUTERS/Aly Song/File Photo\" height=\"2947\" width=\"4421\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>FILE PHOTO: Tesla China-made Model 3 vehicles are seen during a delivery event at its factory in Shanghai\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Tesla's manufacturing has improved by large magnitudes from the days of \"production hell,\" one expert says.&#160;</li>\n<li>Sandy Munro, one of the foremost experts on vehicle teardowns and cost analysis, says the Model Y is the first electric vehicle he's ever recommended.&#160;</li>\n<li>The company improves because it constantly evolves its design, something that's helped it get a decade up on the competition, Munro said in an interview.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>It's been years since Elon Musk was famously sleeping at Tesla's factory amid \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-said-he-slept-on-tesla-factory-floor-to-maximize-suffering-2018-7\">production hell</a>.\"</p><p>And in the time since, things have improved so much that Tesla is now a full decade ahead of the competition, according to one manufacturing expert.</p><p>\"I don't think they really quite understood or grasped the concept of making cars at production speeds,\" Sandy Munro, well-known for his cost analysis teardowns of cars, told a conference hosted by Bernstein last week.</p><p>But things have changed in the years since, something investors and analysts have clearly noted. The company's stock price has soared alongside four consecutive profitable quarters, a first for Tesla.</p><p>How? \"Well number one, they ripped out a lot of robots,\" Munro said. \"I think that Elon thought that somehow robots could take over everything, but in actuality that's been proven wrong in many, many cases.\"</p><p>Musk himself <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/984882630947753984\">admitted</a> in April that, while robots are helpful, \"excessive automation at Tesla was a mistake …. Humans are underrated.\"</p><p>But there's another area where Tesla has a leg up on the competition, Munro says: it continually improves on designs.</p><p>\"So what Tesla's done is it's cranked out a product that's probably 90%, 95% there,\" he said. \"But they've got so many ways of investigating what's going on in each car all the time that the feedback can say 'Hey, what I think what we should do is X. Let's make that engineering change and implement it on the vehicles from here going forward, and if or when a customer has a problem, bingo, we don't know how to solve it or we'll replace the parts.'\"</p><p>\"If I had to make a choice between the two — getting to 95% and then basically waiting until customers complained and then changing things rapidly,\" Munro continued. \"I'd rather take that approach.\"</p><p>That approach seems to be working. Tesla's on track to produce nearly 500,000 cars this year, analysts estimate, in-line with the company's guidance. The company has already released delivery and production numbers for the third quarter, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-beats-expectations-for-third-quarter-vehicle-deliveries-2020-10\">which topped expectations and set a record</a>. Now, with the Model Y beginning to come off the production line, Munro is impressed.</p><p>\"I said in the past that Tesla with the Model 3 was probably five to eight years ahead of everybody else,\" he said, \"and now in some cases I think that in some areas of the car, Tesla is 10 years ahead, especially when it comes to the manufacturing.\"</p><p>Tesla will report its third-quarter financials on October 21.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Leal-Olivas/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>US officials have revived talks about creating an \"air corridor\" between New York City and London, forming an \"air corridor\" between London and New York before the end of November, allowing passengers to travel between the cities with a shortened quarantine period.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-covid-testing-plan-aims-to-open-new-york-london-travel-by-holidays-11602337721\">Wall Street Journal</a> reported that passengers on the route, which is popular for both business and tourist trips, would be tested for COVID-19 both before flying and upon arrival, allowing them to avoid the usual 14-day quarantine.</p><p>They would still have to quarantine, but for less time. Transportation officials and an airline trade group want the period to be reduced to 24 hours, sources told the Journal, but other officials want to maintain a quarantine period of between four and seven days.</p><p>Officials haven't yet decided who would pay for testing, the paper reported.</p><p>Currently, travelers from the UK are only allowed to enter the US if they are US citizens or permanent residents. Meanwhile, travelers from the US must quarantine for 14 days upon arrival in the UK, and are unable to travel onwards to most European countries.</p><p>The average duration of a US visitor's trip to the UK is seven days, <a href=\"https://airlinesuk.org/uk-economy-loses-32m-every-day-as-result-of-no-airbridge-with-the-us/\">John Holland-Kaye</a>, CEO of Heathrow, the UK's largest airport, said in September. As a result, current quarantine rules \"effectively lock these high-spending visitors out of the UK,\" he said.</p><p>He said later in September that he hoped flights would be \"up and running\" by Thanksgiving, November 26, adding that he thought it was \"entirely feasible.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a business</a></em></p><p>The US is also holding talks with German officials about possible air corridors, the Wall Street Journal said.</p><p>However, a Homeland Security official told the Journal that work to \"safely encourage trans-Atlantic travel while mitigating public health risks\" remained in its early stages.</p><p>In September, business leaders urged the British government to create an air bridge between the US and the UK because of <a href=\"https://www.standard.co.uk/business/air-bridge-aviation-travel-corridor-london-new-york-a4552261.html\">fears that the lack of trans-Atlantic travel was preventing business deals</a>.&#160;</p><p>The UK aviation industry also appealed to the government to reopen the travel corridor between the two countries, arguing that the lack of tourists is impacting \"thousands of jobs\" in the restaurant, hospitality, and retail sectors.</p><p>The collapse of air travel between the UK and the US in 2020 will cost about £11 billion ($14.4 billion), <a href=\"https://airlinesuk.org/uk-economy-loses-32m-every-day-as-result-of-no-airbridge-with-the-us/\">Airlines UK estimated in September</a>, with a £3.5 billion ($4.6 billion) loss from class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Blue Origin, the rocket company owned by <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-elon-musk-rivalry-history-timeline-2020-7\">Jeff Bezos</a>, is about to launch a test flight to try out new moon-landing technologies for NASA.</li>\n<li>NASA developed high-precision sensors, software, and a new computer to help spacecraft land in rocky or shadowy areas of the moon or Mars.</li>\n<li>It <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-tipping-point-private-space-exploration-funding-2018-8\">paid Blue Origin $3 million</a> to test those new preparing to launch a suite of new high-precision moon-landing technologies into space for NASA, then test their mettle with a touchdown back on Earth.</p><p>The company's New Shepard rocket is set to lift off from a launchpad in West Texas at 8:35 a.m. CDT on Tuesday. From there, it should rocket 62 miles into the air — reaching the boundary between Earth's atmosphere and outer space — to briefly expose the NASA hardware to the space environment. The rocket will also release a capsule containing cargo for other companies, then descend back to Earth.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6de0a30f4d550011032443?format=jpeg\" alt=\"blue origin new shepard rocket booster landing\" height=\"2249\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The New Shepard booster lands after the vehicle&#39;s sixth consecutive flight Dec. 11, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/directorates/spacetech/NASA_Tipping_Point_Partnership_to_Test_Precision_Lunar_Landing_Tech\" target=\"_blank\">Blue Origin</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>If NASA's sensor systems, computer, and software perform as planned, they should land the rocket safely 12 minutes after launch.</p><p>NASA hopes to one day use the new landing systems it's testing to send human missions to the moon, set up a permanent base there, and eventually land astronauts on the treacherous Martian landscape.</p><p>The larger system is called SPLICE, short for Safe and Precise Landing – Integrated Capabilities Evolution. It's designed to help future moon missions land with better accuracy and safety — no pilot required. It could even enable future spacecraft to land in boulder fields or shadowy craters that thus far have been considered too hazardous for a safe landing. That capability would open up miles of the lunar surface, along with areas on other planets like Mars.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ef54ffbaee6a817a17487e3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"blue origin human lunar landing hls system moon descent national team hires\" height=\"1687\" width=\"2249\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An illustration of lunar-landing hardware for NASA&#39;s Artemis program conceived of by National Team: a business collaboration led by Blue Origin between Lockheed Martin, Northrop Grumman, and Draper.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Blue Origin/National Team</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>\"Testing SPLICE technologies on a suborbital rocket expands the envelope beyond previous lab tests, helicopter field tests, and lower-altitude suborbital rocket tests,\" John Carson, who works on precision landing technology at NASA's Johnson Space Center, said in a <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/directorates/spacetech/NASA_Tipping_Point_Partnership_to_Test_Precision_Lunar_Landing_Tech\">September news release</a>.</p><p>The test flight was originally scheduled for September 24, but Blue Origin scrubbed it, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/blueorigin/status/1309163293957906432\">citing</a> a power-supply issue. The company also canceled its planned second attempt the following day, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/blueorigin/status/1309465743768027136\">saying</a> it needed to \"verify a fix on a technical issue.\"</p><p>This is the first of two flight tests that Blue Origin will conduct through NASA's Tipping Point program, which awarded six private companies a total of $44 million to help push next-generation technologies over the finish line. Blue Origin got $3 million for the project that's culminating in Tuesday's&#160;test launch. The company also received $10 million to test a propulsion system that would use ultra-cold liquid fuels to land a robot on the moon.</p><h2>New sensors and computers to respond to the lunar terrain</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6d1eb50f4d5500110323ac?format=jpeg\" alt=\"nasa blue origin moon landing splice system\" height=\"1080\" width=\"1920\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>NASA&#39;s SPLICE descent and landing computer (foreground) undergoes preparations for a flight test.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/directorates/spacetech/NASA_Tipping_Point_Partnership_to_Test_Precision_Lunar_Landing_Tech\" target=\"_blank\">Blue Origin</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The Blue Origin flight will only test some elements of the SPLICE technology suite: two sensor systems, landing algorithms, and a new computer.</p><p>The first set of sensors is meant to help spacecraft navigate the terrain where they might land. The system could enable a moon lander to determine its exact location by comparing real-time data from its camera to a set of surface maps pre-uploaded to the computer.</p><p>The other sensor system, a Doppler lidar, is designed to beam lasers to the surface of a planet and use the returning reflections to calculate the spacecraft's landing speed and altitude. This system is slated to fly on two commercial lunar robotic missions in 2021, including the lander that will carry <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-picks-astrobotic-deliver-viper-moon-rover-lunar-ice-2020-6\">NASA's new rover to the moon</a> — the first such landing since the Apollo program ended in 1972.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ee258b52618b92ce7025387?format=jpeg\" alt=\"astrobotic griffin moon lander lunar rover viper\" height=\"1462\" width=\"1950\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An illustration shows Astrobotic&#39;s Griffin lunar lander deploying a ramp on the moon&#39;s surface.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.astrobotic.com/media-kit/images\" target=\"_blank\">Astrobotic</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>NASA designed the new technologies so they could work together or separately, allowing the agency to pick and choose the elements required for particular missions. The Blue Origin flight will test how the elements work together in a new spacecraft.</p><p>\"The sensor data is all processed via the descent and landing computer,\" Carson said. \"Lots of other software runs in the background, integrating the different systems, figuring out what needs to run next, and, for this test, synchronizing timing with the Blue Origin flight computer. It's all crucial so the system can run autonomously and provide us with data that we can analyze post-flight.\"</p><p>NASA plans to trial a third sensor system — which would scan the surface of a planet to detect hazards and choose safer landing spots — in future testing.</p><p>Here is Blue Origin's live feed of the test flight, which will start broadcasting 30 minutes before launch:&#160;</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/O97dPDkUGg4\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p>&#160;</p><p>NASA will also air the event on its live broadcast:</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/21X5lGlDOfg\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p><em>Dave Mosher contributed reporting.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/blue-origin-launch-nasa-moon-landing-technology-2020-9'>Business href=\"https://www.insider.com/la-lakers-stars-pay-tribute-kobe-bryant-nba-title-win-2020-10\">led the Los Angeles Lakers</a> to a record-equaling 17th NBA championship on Sunday night. Warren Buffett, a longtime fan and confidant of the basketball superstar, once used James' outsized contribution to his team to explain the danger of diversification for investors.</p><p>\"If you have LeBron James on your team, don't take him out of the game just to make room for someone else,\" the billionaire investor and Berkshire Hathaway CEO told a group of business-school students in 2008.</p><p>\"It's crazy to put money into your 20th choice, rather than your first choice,\" Buffett added, <a href=\"https://undergroundvalue.blogspot.com/2008/02/notes-from-buffett-meeting-2152008_23.html\">according to Dang Le</a>, one of the students in attendance.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">:&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-companies-with-best-profit-growth-goldman-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-companies-with-best-profit-growth-goldman-2020-10\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">GOLDMAN SACHS: Buy these 15 stocks set to deliver the strongest possible profit growth and subsequent returns through year-end</a></em></p><p>Buffett has embraced that approach at Berkshire. Its five biggest holdings — Apple, Bank of America, Coca-Cola, American Express, and Kraft Heinz — account for more than 75% of its roughly $200 billion stock portfolio.</p><p>On another occasion, the investor compared James' return to his hometown team, the Cleveland Cavaliers, to Coca-Cola's reversion to its classic formula.</p><p>\"He loves Cleveland, Cleveland loves him,\" Buffett said in 2014, <a href=\"https://www.cleveland.com/cavs/2014/12/warren_buffett_lebron_james.html\">according to cleveland.com</a>. \"In a sense, it's like new Coke and old Coke.\"</p><p>\"Years ago they were going to take away the old Coke so they could make a new Coke, and then all of a sudden everyone remembered how much they loved the old Coke,\" he continued. \"That's the way this is.\"</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">:&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-spac-etf-spak-benefits-risks-for-retail-investors-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-spac-etf-spak-benefits-risks-for-retail-investors-2020-10\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">SPACs have generated a $39 billion frenzy in the US this year. The executive behind their first ETF explains how retail investors can use them to level the playing field with Wall Street titans like Warren Buffett.</a></em></p><p>Buffett and James first met when the athlete visited Omaha to shoot a skit for Berkshire's annual meeting in 2007. The pair have been mutual admirers since then.</p><p>\"I'm a kid from Akron who lived in poverty for a long time, and sometimes I send financial statements to one of the richest guys ever,\" James <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lebron-financial-statements-warren-buffett-2012-12?utm_source=msn.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=msn-slideshow&utm_campaign=bodyurl&r=US&IR=Trl&#38;r=US&#38;IR=T\">told Sports Illustrated in 2012</a>.</p><p>\"It's kind of scary,\" he continued. \"I'm like, 'Why is he talking to me?'\"</p><p>Meanwhile, Buffett praised James' maturity in a <a href=\"https://www.miamiherald.com/sports/nba/article1944185.html\">Miami Herald interview</a> in 2012, and the player's \"money mind\", or financial savvy, in a <a href=\"https://eu.usatoday.com/story/sports/nba/lakers/2018/10/02/warren-buffet-praises-lebron-james-his-money-mind/1503360002/\">USA Today interview</a> in 2018.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read Mike Lee speaks without a mask at Monday&#39;s opening hearing for President Trump&#39;s Supreme Court nominee, Amy Coney Barrett.\n<p class=\"copyright\">ALEX EDELMAN/POOL/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Republican Sen. Mike Lee of Utah drew suspicion and ire on Monday when he spoke maskless at the first Senate Judiciary Committee hearing for President Donald Trump's Supreme Court nominee Amy Coney Barrett.</li>\n<li>Lee tested positive for COVID-19 on Friday, October 2, with his case being one of many linked to an apparent superspreader event at the White House Rose Garden for Barrett about a week earlier.</li>\n<li>The senator would not tell reporters if he tested negative for the virus before showing up to the hearing room, but he did tweet a letter from his doctor that \"cleared\" him for an in-person cameo.</li>\n<li>\"Senator Lee's enthusiasm for the dormant commerce clause convinces me you've made a full recovery,\" Sen. Mike Lee, R-Utah, spoke without a mask at the first confirmation hearing for Supreme Court nominee Amy Coney Barrett, 10 days after testing positive for coronavirus.</p><p>Lee's case was one of many linked to Barrett's nomination ceremony at the White House Rose Garden on Sept. 26, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/rose-garden-ceremony-barrett-coronavirus-superspreading-event-2020-10\">which appears to check all the boxes for a superspreader event</a>.</p><p>On Monday, the senator declined to tell reporters if he tested negative for the virus, but tweeted a letter from his doctor declaring him \"cleared\" to attend the hearing in person despite the ability to make statements and ask questions remotely.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Mike Lee  (@SenMikeLee) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1315663162310643713?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 12, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>In the letter Lee posted, Dr. Brian Monahan, the attending physician of the Congress, ruled out testing as a factor for the senator's return to Capitol Hill.</p><p>\"Based upon current CDC guidelines, you have met criteria to end COVID-19 isolation for those with mild to moderate disease,\" Monahan wrote to Lee. \"Specifically, it has been greater than 10 days since symptom onset, you have had no fever in absence of fever reducing medication for at least 24 hours, and your other symptoms have improved. The CDC does not recommend repeat SARS-CoV-2 PCR testing if these criteria are met.\"</p><p>This was echoed by Amesh Adalja, a senior scholar at the Johns Hopkins University Center for Health Security.</p><p>\"We don't test people to say they're non-infectious,\" Adalja told Business Insider. \"We wait 10 days and say: Are they better? Have their symptoms decreased? Are they not having a fever for the last three days and not taking Tylenol or ibuprofen? And then we release them.\"</p><p>Lee's lack of transparency over whether he's contagious and still testing positive for the virus drew concerns online.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Manu Raju  (@mkraju) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1315658057377026048?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 12, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Lisa Desjardins  (@LisaDNews) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1315638902468739072?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 12, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>But Senate Judiciary Chairman Sen. years","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-bans-holocaust-denial-posts-after-refusing-removal-content-moderation-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f846904642e9400180b5530?format=jpeg\" alt=\"facebook mark zuckerberg\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg appears before a House Financial Services Committee hearing on Capitol Hill in Washington, Wednesday, Oct. 23, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Harnik/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Facebook announced Monday it was changing its hate speech policy to \"prohibit any content that denies or distorts the Holocaust.\"</li>\n<li>The company has faced criticism for more than a decade over its refusal to moderate anti-Semitic content that distorts or denies the Holocaust, when Nazis and their allies systematically killed 6 million Jews, happened.</li>\n<li>In the weeks leading up to the 2020 presidential election, Facebook has attempted to mitigate criticism that it fails to prevent the spread of dangerous conspiracy theories and disinformation on its platform. Just last week, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/qanon-banned-from-facebook-dealing-massive-blow-to-conspiracy-group-2020-10\">Facebook said it banned QAnon</a> accounts across its platforms.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook has banned Holocaust-denial content from the platform after years of criticism over its refusal to take action against such anti-Semitic rhetoric.</p><p><a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/removing-holocaust-denial-content/\">Facebook announced Monday</a> it was updating its hate speech policy to \"prohibit any content that denies or distorts the Holocaust.\"</p><p>The policy change marks an abrupt about-face on Facebook's refusal, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2010/12/13/technology/13facebook.html\">for more than a decade</a>, to remove content from its platform that denies the existence of the Holocaust and the genocide of millions of Jews and other minority groups. The platform has faced pressure from human rights and civil rights groups to take a stricter stance against such content, but <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/Technology/AheadoftheCurve/story?id=7566812&page=1ge=1\">Facebook has maintained that</a> the \"mere statement\" of Holocaust denial doesn't violate policies.</p><p>\"I'm Jewish, and there's a set of people who deny that the Holocaust happened. I find that deeply offensive,\" <a href=\"https://www.recode.net/2018/7/18/17575156/mark-zuckerberg-interview-facebook-recode-kara-swisher\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"eca9c651127cf661415d5cd46e709fae\">CEO Mark Zuckerberg told Recode in July 2018</a>. \"But at the end of the day, I don't believe that our platform should take that down because I think there are things that different people get wrong.\"</p><p>In the meantime, it appears that Holocaust-denial content on Facebook has continued to not just exist, but flourish. <a href=\"https://www.isdglobal.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Hosting-the-Holohoax.pdf\">A recent study</a>, published in August by the British think tank Institute for Strategic Dialogue, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-actively-promotes-holocaust-denial-content-study-finds-2020-8\">found that Facebook</a> \"actively promotes\" Holocaust denial content to users who had previously interacted with such material on the platform.</p><p>Critics of Facebook say the company has failed to moderate its platform and prevent the spread of dangerous misinformation and conspiracy theories. A <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/facebook-knows-it-encourages-division-top-executives-nixed-solutions-11590507499?mod=searchresults&page=1&pos=1mp;pos=1\">report from The Wall Street Journal</a> earlier this year revealed that Facebook executives knew its platforms' algorithms encourage divisiveness — and chose to not do anything to change it.</p><p>But in the weeks ahead of the 2020 presidential election, it appears Facebook is trying to show it's cracking down. The company announced last week it was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/qanon-banned-from-facebook-dealing-massive-blow-to-conspiracy-group-2020-10\">banning accounts related to the conspiracy theory QAnon</a>, which has become a rallying point for some on the far right and led to violence.</p><p><em>Got a tip? chief economic advisor at Allianz, said Monday.</p><p>After a brief bout of calmed market volatility, choppy trading resumed earlier this month after President Donald Trump abruptly canceled, and just as surprisingly revived, plans for another stimulus package. While Democrats and the White House have inched closer to reaching a compromise, Senate Republicans have balked at all recent proposals.</p><p>Investors continue to tell themselves \"it's a matter of time\" before Congress passes another massive spending package, El-Erian said on <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/video/2020/10/12/el-erian-markets-investment-strategy-stimulus-squawk-box.html\">CNBC</a>. Though deal progress has been made in recent weeks, the market's rally rests on an uneasy foundation, he added.</p><p>\"The problem with the 'it's a matter of time' argument is there's ongoing damage to the economy every day, so it really does matter when this will come,\" he said. \"This market is completely behavioral. It wants to go up and then it finds the narrative to justify why it's gone up.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-expert-foresees-drop-massive-financial-crisis-bankruptcies-2020-10\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"\">'The largest financial crisis in history': A 47-year market vet says the COVID-19 crash was merely a 'fake-out sell-off' — and warns of an 80% stock plunge fraught with bank failures and bankruptcies</a></em></p><p>He continued: \"This market will look at whatever silver linings there are, on the stimulus, and extrapolate that.\"</p><p>The window to pass a package is quickly closing. Senate Republicans are focused on confirming Amy Coney Barrett to the Supreme Court, placing fiscal relief talks on the party's back-burner. Once confirmation hearings end on Thursday, legislators have just two weeks to finalize a deal before Election Day.</p><p>No matter how much investors focus on economic data or Wall Street projections, progress on a spending bill is \"the only thing that matters this week\" to the market's trajectory, El-Erian said.</p><p>The stimulus impasse comes as economic indicators slow their pace of recovery and suggest some damage will linger until well after the coronavirus pandemic ends. Jobless claims data published Thursday showed claims <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-jobless-claims-weekly-unemployment-insurance-benefits-hiring-economic-recovery-2020-10\">falling slightly to 840,000</a>, still sitting well above the worst readings seen during the Great Recession. Gauges of consumer spending have slowed their return to pre-pandemic highs.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stocks-to-buy-4-companies-long-term-volatility-jd-gardner-2020-10\" data-analytics-position=\"5\" data-analytics-module=\"\">A $2 billion fund manager says market volatility is here to stay for the long-term. He breaks down his best recommendations for the new normal — including 4 of his favorite stocks.</a></em></p><p>New daily COVID-19 cases have also trended higher in recent weeks, reviving fears of widespread lockdowns.</p><p>The trendline&#160;of economic recovery is starting to look less like the sought-after V-shape and more like a square-root sign, El-Erian said.</p><p>\"You come back up and you flatten too early. Too early relative to what it could be and too early relative to what we need,\" he added.</p><p>To be sure, the US has yet to suffer a crippling wave of corporate bankruptcies. Markets boast enough liquidity and investor demand to offer cheap financing to cash-strapped firms. href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/taco-bell-nixes-mexican-pizza-adds-chicken-chipotle-melt-2020-9\">Taco Bell announced its plans</a> to axe the Mexican Pizza, as well as pico de gallo and shredded chicken, in September. The Mexican Pizza is set to permanently disappear from menus on November 5, making room for new options including the Chicken Chipotle Melt and Dragonfruit Freeze.&#160;</p><p>In the weeks since, fans of Taco Bell's Mexican Pizza have taken to social media to mourn their loss — and strategize about plans to keep the pizza on the menu.&#160;</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><blockquote class=\"tiktok-embed\" cite=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@eatitkatie/video/6869118681868176645\" data-video-id=\"6869118681868176645\" style=\"max-width: 605px;min-width: 325px;\" > <section> <a target=\"_blank\" title=\"@eatitkatie\" href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@eatitkatie\">@eatitkatie</a> <p>First fiesta potatoes and now THIS?!
