class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Election Day is 22 days away.</li>\n<li>Already, Democratic nominee Joe Biden leads President Donald Trump by 10.5 points in an average of 2020 presidential election polls from <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/polls/president-general/national/\">FiveThirtyEight</a>.</li>\n<li>Over 9.5 million people have already voted across the United States and voting experts predict that mail-in voting will make up more than 50% of the overall vote.</li>\n<li>As millions continue to cast early votes, the window to convince undecided voters is quickly closing.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>With just over three weeks to go until the Election Day on November 3, Democratic nominee Joe Biden leads President Donald Trump by 10.5 percentage points, according to an average of polls by <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/polls/president-general/national/\">FiveThirtyEight</a>.</p><p>At this point in the 2016 election, Democratic nominee Hillary Clinton was 6.9 percentage points ahead of Trump, <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/2016-election-forecast/national-polls/\">FiveThirtyEight</a> found.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/10/11/politics/biden-best-position-challenger/index.html\">According to CNN</a>, in the 21 presidential elections held since 1936, only five challengers to the sitting president led at this point in the race. Of those five, only Bill Clinton led by more than 5 points. Biden is the first challenger to an incumbent president to poll above 50% this late in the campaign.\"</p><p>After a contentious battle in the first presidential debate on September 29, the Trump campaign wanted nothing more than to jump back onto the campaign trail and drum up support before the election. Instead, a major wrench was thrown into the plan: Trump tested <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-coronavirus-condition-had-congestion-in-lungs-2020-10\">positive for COVID-19</a> and wound up in hospital.</p><p>The president's diagnosis prompted the Commission on Presidential Debates to change the second debate's format from in-person to virtual. But this <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-second-debate-with-biden-will-be-remote-commission-says-2020-10\">displeased Trump</a> and he backed out. Both Trump and Biden will now host <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/10/11/media/trump-biden-town-halls/index.html\">town halls</a> on October 15 instead.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Aaron Rupar  (@atrupar) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1314174756430774273?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 8, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>After being sidelined at Walter Reed National Military Medical Center and sequestered to the White House to recover, Trump's window to win over undecided voters is quickly closing.</p><p>As it currently stands, the Trump campaign is failing to win over the female vote. According to the&#160;<a href=\"https://cawp.rutgers.edu/presidential-poll-tracking-2020\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"6c1990d4737adc9176479add75d46ceb\">Center for American Women and Politics</a> at Rutgers University, Biden leads among women voters by an average of 18.6 percentage points in the 46 national polls tracked by the organization.</p><p>While Trump struggles to gain the trust of women voters, Biden has consistently struggled to win over Cuban-American voters in Florida, a state that he needs to win for an easier path to the Oval Office. Florida is home to nearly two-thirds of the nation's 1.2 million eligible Cuban-American voters, who were about <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/11/15/unlike-other-latinos-about-half-of-cuban-voters-in-florida-backed-trump/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"d7955d5adde307caeba015a23cf685c3\">twice as likely</a> to vote for Trump in 2016 than non-Cuban Latinos in the state.</p><p>While his polling numbers within this group are improving, Biden still trails Trump by 26 points, according to a recent poll from <a href=\"https://www.miamiherald.com/news/politics-government/article246216955.html\">Bendixen &#38; Amandi International and the Miami Herald</a>.</p><p>Since the death of Supreme Court Justice Ruth Bader Ginsburg, the Trump campaign's apparent hope is that the nomination of Judge Amy Coney Barrett to the Supreme Court will push Republican voters to the polls. That push, however, may be for naught as an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/insider-poll-52-of-conservatives-want-scotus-pick-pre-election-2020-9?fbclid=IwAR0fci3JL_JlUe3ah17a-UFmyDGe958eo-a9tO0QjtEHpPr8DKl-GxRZwRE\">Insider poll</a> from late September shows only 52% of conservative voters think the open seat should be filled before the election.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Dana Bash  (@DanaBashCNN) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1308417205248364546?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 22, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>As of October 12, over <a href=\"https://electproject.github.io/Early-Vote-2020G/index.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"92235dcf49c8479097fa7c34970cf487\">9 million ballots</a> have already been cast through <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/when-is-early-voting-in-each-state-2020-8\">early and mail-in voting</a>. At this point in 2016, <a href=\"http://www.electproject.org/early_2016\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"87fe344aa09337f91a2aa54ef72f5e18\">only 430,000 mail-in votes</a> had been cast. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/america-likely-wont-know-presidential-race-winner-on-election-night-2020-5\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"1e9ae4f6973e5e60f4f470f70336a2d3\">Voting rights experts</a> anticipate voting by mail to make up 50% to 70% of the total vote in November.</p><p>If Biden or Trump wishes to make significant polling or electorate gains before the election, they must act now — the longer they wait, the more early votes they stand to lose.</p><bi-shortcode 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"This video chat app that's like Zoom for kids wants to make virtual babysitting the next big thing","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/caribu-app-reading-bedtime-stories-boomed-during-covid-19-pandemic-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f64f745323fc4001e0d72c1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Caribu CEO Headshot\" height=\"2014\" width=\"2681\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Maxeme Tuchman, CEO of Caribu\n<p class=\"copyright\">Caribu</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Caribu, an app that lets parents and grandparents read bedtime stories to their children and grandkids virtually, boomed during the pandemic.</li>\n<li>The app grew tenfold in March, and now its co-founder Maxeme Tuchman says its expanding to the classroom and the home office.</li>\n<li>Now, the company is pushing for some employers to offer Caribu as a benefit, which could be helpful for parents working from home with young kids.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>If you're familiar with Maxeme Tuchman's background, you wouldn't be surprised to hear she runs a company that promotes reading and education among children.</p><p>Tuchman spent more than two years as the executive director of Teach for America's Miami-Dade branch starting in 2013. She also previously managed education projects under Michael Bloomberg, the former mayor of New York City, and Michelle Ree, the former D.C. public schools chancellor.</p><p>But it wasn't until 2016 that Tuchman and her co-founder began building Caribu, a video calling app on iOS, Android, and the web that lets children read and play games with family members remotely.</p><p>In fact, the idea originated from a photo the two came across of a soldier video-chatting on a laptop in a coffee shop.&#160;</p><p>\"You see him holding up this huge picture book and facing it toward the laptop,\" Tuchman said to Business Insider. \"There should be better technology in this day and age for families who are distant from their kids to be able to share that ritual of reading a bedtime story together.\"</p><p>While the app may be best known for its wide selection of children's books that adults and children can read together virtually, Caribu also offers coloring sheets, games, drawing tools, and recipes that kids and relatives can cook together. The app comes with 15 free books or activities per calendar month and offers unlimited access for $10 per month, or $100 per year.</p><p>The company says the app is being used in more than 200 countries and territories around the world.&#160;</p><p>Caribu may not be new, but it boomed in 2020 as grandparents, aunts, and uncles were unable to visit their grandkids, nieces, and nephews for months in the pandemic's early days. The app grew by more than half a million users during the pandemic, the company says.&#160;</p><p>According to Tuchman, this was a tenfold increase that occured overnight.</p><p>\"You could say that I haven't slept since March 13,\" Tuchman said.</p><p>It's no surprise that an app like Caribu would see increased demand at a time when children were unable to attend playdates with friends, attend school in person, or visit relatives. After all, video conferencing tools like Zoom, Microsoft Teams, and Google Meet also saw a massive uptick in the first half of 2020.</p><p>Tuchman is confident that Caribu will continue to grow and is starting to pitch Caribu as an employer benefit, which can be useful for parents who may begin working remotely permanently even after the pandemic. Caribu couldn't disclose the companies it's working with to potentially offer its service as a benefit, but it did say they include financial services companies and startups.&#160;&#160;</p><p>There certainly appears to be interest in more flexible work arrangements that include at least some remote work. Even when the coronavirus is no longer a top concern, 83% of office workers say they want to work from home at least one day per week, according to a June <a href=\"https://www.pwc.com/us/en/library/covid-19/us-remote-work-survey.html\">survey from PwC</a>.&#160;</p><p>Plus, large tech firms like Twitter and Shopify have said that they will allow employees to work remotely permanently if they wish.&#160;&#160;</p><p>\"You don't need access to a gym right now,\" Tuchman said. \"You don't need access to a happy hour every Friday. You don't need free snacks. You need something like Caribu which is virtual babysitting.\"</p><p>Those digital tools are becoming increasingly important for parents and relatives who may be home-schooling their children this year.</p><p>The company also recently launched Caribu on the web and made its subscription free to teachers for the 2020-2021 school year so they can use it as a tool in virtual classrooms this fall.&#160;</p><p>Interaction that includes a lot of back-and-forth participation can be crucial for developing children's social skills, according to Kathryn Hirsh-Pasek, a senior fellow at the Brookings Institution and a faculty fellow in Temple University's psychology department.&#160;</p><p>When reading to children, for example, parents, grandparents, and teachers don't just read the text — they connect the story to real-life experiences. Continuing these types of interactions even in virtual environments is important, Hirsh-Pasek said.</p><p>\"I like to think of it as going beyond the cover,\" Hirsh-Pasek said. \"We ask questions like, 'Oh, remember we saw a monkey at the zoo? Curious George is a monkey like that.' And the minute you connect it to personal experiences and personal narratives, you have significantly broadened the power of the interaction.\"</p><p>COVID-19 changes aside, there are always going to be frequently-traveling parents or long-distance relatives looking for ways to keep in touch with the kids in their lives, Tuchman said.</p><p>\"We help people stay connected and feel connected and feel like they're together even when they can't be,\" Tuchman said. \"We've existed in a pre-pandemic world too.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a for loose items other than door pockets or the cupholders, neither of which are ideal. The RAV4's are an excellent use of what otherwise would have been dead space.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/toyota-rav4\">Toyota RAV4</a> — a brilliant, highly utilitarian car recently made even more efficient with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/toyota-rav4-prime-plug-in-hybrid-specs-pricing-release-date-2020-6\">a plug-in hybrid offering</a> — has one of the greatest interior features I've ever come across in a car. And it's not even an optional feature you have to pay extra for. It comes standard.</p><p>Essentially, it's this: a handy little cubby introduced with the <a href=\"https://jalopnik.com/the-2019-toyota-rav4-can-almost-do-it-all-1834282110\">current-generation RAV4</a>, which has been around for a few model years now.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f809dc5ea74820019ca6439?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2021 Toyota RAV4 XSE AWD_KL_32\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Look, I&#39;m creature of simple taste. Love me a good cubby.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kristen Lee/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>\"What's the big deal?\" you snort to yourself. \"Plenty of cars have cubbies.\"</p><p>But do they actually? Or are you just dumping all your knick-knacks into a cupholder and calling it a day?</p><p>It's true that cupholders are for drinks, but drinks aren't the only loose items we bring into cars. Most of us are forced to stick phones, wallets, sunglasses, pens, change, keys, lip balm, moisturizer, garage key cards, charging cables, hand sanitizer, face masks, ketchup packets, and vapes (hey, I don't know your life) into whatever free space we can find in our cars for safekeeping while we drive.</p><p>More often than not, stuff ends up in the cupholders.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f809dc5ea74820019ca643c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2021 Toyota RAV4 XSE AWD_KL_64\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>What would you put here?\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kristen Lee/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>For its fifth and current generation, the RAV4 does away with that forced packing. It gives us two rubber-lined cubbies that run along the dashboard. There's a long one for the front passenger and a short one for the driver, and it's a wonderful use of otherwise dead space.</p><p>In the 10 or so days that I spent with the RAV4 Prime — which was excellent, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/rav4-toyota-plug-in-hybrid-first-drive-review-suv-mpg-2020-10\">you should read the full review</a> — I made full use of those cubbies. As everyone who carries a purse knows, you don't always want to take it with you everywhere, especially if you're just running out for a quick errand.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f809dc4ea74820019ca6436?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2021 Toyota RAV4 XSE AWD_KL_37\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>This is perfect for car keys or a phone.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kristen Lee/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Sometimes you just want to bring your wallet and your phone. Both of these fit perfectly in the cubby, as does the RAV4's key. The cubby is also far more convenient than putting things in door pockets, since those tend to be deep and it's easy to forget you've put something there.</p><p>The RAV4's cubbies are eye-level so you can easily see if you've left anything there. The rubber lining makes them both easy to clean and able to keep the items you put there from sliding around so much. A little lip helps prevent&#160;things from rolling out onto the floor.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f80c9cd4c3b2e0019bba4b3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2018_Toyota_RAV4_Adventure_18_C37AC3A0E0DB83995045655A6EBA83522CB28268\" height=\"1431\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The interior of the previous-gen RAV4: Cubby-less. Barren. Sad.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Toyota</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>It's thoughtful little touches such as these that tell me that someone designed this RAV4's interior to be used by real people. Real people carry stuff with them, and that stuff needs a place to go.</p><p>With the RAV4, you can have a spot for your stuff <em>and </em>both you and your passenger can still have a cupholder apiece. You can have your cake and eat it, too.</p><p>The next time I get into a cramped sports car with zero storage space — where I've wedged my wallet between the seat and the door, I'm sitting on my phone, and the keys are God knows where — I'll be thinking back wistfully to a cubby-lined RAV4 that treated me right.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f809e1fea74820019ca6458?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2021 Toyota RAV4 XSE AWD_OEM_2\" height=\"1668\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>I left my heart in the rubber-lined cubby of a 2021 Toyota RAV4 Prime.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Toyota</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a :"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=aYQrwElZFD0:6yS3hgbg-Vc:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn10@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-55-817_5985188aa260dceb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=aYQrwElZFD0:6yS3hgbg-Vc:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn65@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-52-798_463e6c9565684a20.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=aYQrwElZFD0:6yS3hgbg-Vc:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn47@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-55-421_792b367bb0a96fb6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/aYQrwElZFD0":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289930},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"Scammers are sending fake texts about FedEx and USPS packages, and it's fueling a conspiracy theory about a sex trafficking scandal","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/fedex-usps-package-scam-texts-not-linked-to-sex-trafficking","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f411e4842f43f001ddfe7de?format=jpeg\" alt=\"USPS\" height=\"3414\" width=\"4552\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A USPS mail worker wearing a mask wheels a priority mail and Amazon package near a USPS truck as the city continues Phase 4 of re-opening following restrictions imposed to slow the spread of coronavirus on August 20, 2020 in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alexi Rosenfeld/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>People across the country are reporting getting spam texts that appear to be from the USPS, FedEx, and UPS.</li>\n<li>The FTC and Better Business Bureau have warned against clicking links in these messages.</li>\n<li>Despite social media claims, there is no evidence the texts are linked to sex trafficking.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>People across the US are getting text messages as part of a phishing scheme that claims to be giving updates about a package from USPS, UPS, or FedEx. Some viral social media posts have claimed that these messages are related to a sex trafficking operation that uses the links to track potential victims, though there is no evidence behind those claims.</p><p>Texts come from a random unknown number, claiming some problem with a package delivery, usually something needing urgent attention like an \"important alert\" or \"final notice.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f847fb6c255d800190b94d8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"USPS text scam\" height=\"620\" width=\"827\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Spam text.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mary Meisenzahl/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The messages are easy to mistake for genuine updates. In many cases, they have the correct first name of the recipient, and include potentially legitimate information that might seem real, like a tracking number. Clicking the link is supposed to help resolve the issue with the package, but it actually just infects a device with malware, <a href=\"https://gizmodo.com/no-usps-spam-isnt-secretly-tracking-your-phone-1845066490\">Shoshana Wodinsky at Gizmodo reported</a>. Information security researched <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SlickRockWeb/status/1305900305113116674\">Eric Ellason</a> wrote a Twitter thread explaining how the scam works.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Eric JN Ellason  (@SlickRockWeb) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1305900305113116674?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 15, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>In other cases, the scammer behind the phony text is after other security information, including a credit card number or social security number.</p><p>These scams are common enough that the <a href=\"https://www.bbb.org/article/scams/16460-scam-alert-fake-text-delivery-scam\">Better Business Bureau</a>&#160;and <a href=\"https://www.consumer.ftc.gov/blog/2020/02/text-message-about-your-fedex-package-really-scam?_ga=2.230171868.1166097783.1600090605-1623916963.1600090604\">FTC</a> both put out alerts earlier this year warning people, with tips on how to avoid getting scammed. As a general rule, the FTC advises \"If you get an unexpected text message, don't click on any links. If you think it could be legit, contact the company using a website or phone number you know is real. Don't use the information in the text message.\"</p><p>Phishing attempts like these texts are particularly nefarious because many of these companies do send out legitimate alerts that look quite similar. <a href=\"https://www.usps.com/text-tracking/welcome.htm\">USPS</a>, <a href=\"http://www.fedex.com/in/small-business/sms-tracking.html\">FedEx</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.ups.com/us/en/help-center/tracking-support/sms-track.page\">UPS</a> each have SMS update options, though consumers have to proactively sign up for them. To further add to the confusion, these companies will also send texts about delivery times and delays, although authentic messages will consistently come from the same number. Signing up for alerts isn't necessarily a bad idea either, as consumers order expensive electronics for delivery from Apple or Amazon, for example.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8483cb91aa9e001880afc9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"smsUSPS\" height=\"1790\" width=\"2387\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Real delivery alerts.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mary Meisenzahl/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>These scams are also hard to spot because, at any given time, there's a good chance you might be waiting on a package. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-ecommerce-sales-grew-by-nearly-a-third-q2-2020-8\">Ecommerce sales</a> increased by nearly a third in Q2 as the pandemic kept many people inside and online shopping became more convenient than ever. With a year over year increased of 44.5%, ecommerce is a $211.5 billion industry.&#160;</p><p>Consumer protection agencies are in agreement that these texts are a scam, but some social media posts claim that they're a different type of danger. As the <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/9/15/21438661/qanon-usps-phishing-scam\">Verge</a> and <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/usps-text-scam-fake-package-sex-trafficking-2020-9\">Insider</a> reported, now deleted Instagram posts stated that the texts were part of a threat where sex traffickers gained access to a device's location through the link.</p><p>The organization behind the US National Sex Trafficking Hotline, <a href=\"https://polarisproject.org/press-releases/polaris-statement-regarding-rumors-about-unclaimed-package-text-messages-and-sex-trafficking-scheme/\">Polaris</a>, put out a statement clarifying that there is no evidence connecting these spam messages with human trafficking. However, the debunked theory continues to circulate on Instagram, Twitter, and Facebook.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/fedex-usps-package-scam-texts-not-linked-to-sex-trafficking'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 2020 16:53:53 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f411e4842f43f001ddfe7de?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"abe1c20c9f125f87a3f3da4013bff3c6","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn25@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-50-720_97d999b21afa94a9.webp","destWidth":4552,"destHeight":3414,"sourceBytes":633726,"destBytes":633726,"author":"mmeisenzahl@businessinsider.com (Mary Meisenzahl)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f411e4842f43f001ddfe7de?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn25@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-50-720_97d999b21afa94a9.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f847fb6c255d800190b94d8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn44@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-57-745_c81afb1b1f20689f.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8483cb91aa9e001880afc9?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn77@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-05-02-373_64408047c71bc633.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=7TsTzsklMmQ:EIFsYBFiuV8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=7TsTzsklMmQ:EIFsYBFiuV8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn6@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-57-418_ee0fdca9736eebcc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=7TsTzsklMmQ:EIFsYBFiuV8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn23@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-05-03-630_94585b5be3b65d7c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/7TsTzsklMmQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn9@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-56-748_70c63aeac1add37c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289939},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"A study finds new moms with COVID-19 do not need to be separated from their babies after birth — but they should wear masks","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-moms-covid-very-low-risk-transmission-to-babies-study-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e1e408049878c2a2a20dad5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"newborn in hospital\" height=\"3600\" width=\"5400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>COVID-positive new moms don't necessarily need to be separated from their babies after birth in order to prevent transmission, the most detailed study on the topic to date suggests.&#160;</li>\n<li>Good hygiene, mask-wearing, and social distancing while resting seem to effective in keeping babies safe while also allowing them to benefit from breastfeeding and skin-to-skin contact.&#160;</li>\n<li>While two of the 101 babies studied tested positive for COVID, they were asymptomatic and healthy. Past research shows even strict post-birth prevention measures don't always prevent transmission.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Separating a new mom with the coronavirus from her baby immediately after birth may not be necessary in order to protect the infant from COVID-19, according to the most detailed study on transmission of the novel coronavirus between moms and babies to date.&#160;</p><p>In fact, the tactic — used in some hospitals per the guidance of some pediatric and health organizations when less was known about the risks COVID-positive moms may pose to their newborns — may do more harm than good by, for example, discouraging breastfeeding, the study, published today in <a href=\"https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamapediatrics/fullarticle/2771636\">JAMA Pediatrics</a>, suggests.&#160;</p><p>\"Some of the [prior] recommendations conflict with what we know about the developmental benefits of early breastfeeding and skin-to-skin contact,\" lead author Dr. Dani Dumitriu, an assistant professor of pediatrics in psychiatry at Columbia University Vagelos College of Physicians and Surgeons, said in a press release.&#160;&#160;</p><p>\"Our study shows that these measures may not be necessary for healthy newborns with COVID-positive moms.\"</p><h2>Only 2 of 101 infants studied were COVID-positive, but had no symptoms and remained healthy</h2><p>For the study, researchers looked at 101 infants who were born to moms with COVID-19 between March 13 and April 24 at two NewYork-Presbyterian hospitals.&#160;</p><p>Most moms and infants weren't separated after birth, though some needed to, for example, if the babies needed intensive care due to non-COVID related issues.&#160;</p><p>For those who remained together, the hospital implemented other COVID transmission prevention measures like putting the pair in private rooms where the babies stayed in protective cribs six feet away when resting.&#160;</p><p>Hospital staffers also practiced social distancing, wore masks, and discharged the women earlier than typical if they didn't have complications requiring a longer stay.&#160;</p><p>Moms were also strongly encouraged to breastfeed and initiate skin-to-skin contact, so long as they wore masks and washed their hands and breasts.</p><p>Two of the newborns tested positive for SARS-CoV-2, but didn't have any symptoms. Two weeks later, they remained in good health.&#160;&#160;</p><p>\"Our findings should reassure expectant mothers with COVID-19 that basic infection-control measures during and after childbirth ... protected newborns from infection in this series,\" senior author Dr. Cynthia Gyamfi-Bannerman, a maternal-fetal medicine expert at NewYork-Presbyterian said in the press release.&#160;</p><p>\"We think it's particularly important that mothers with COVID-19 have the opportunity to directly breastfeed their newborns,\" she added, noting that breast milk may protect newborns against the coronavirus.&#160;</p><h2>It's unclear how the two babies with COVID contracted the illness&#160;</h2><p>Most research to date suggests COVID-19 is unlikely to be transmitted in utero.&#160;</p><p>One<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/a-small-new-study-suggests-the-coronavirus-damages-the-placenta-2020-5?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"49c353b64229707d5d3cc3ebc79c1c0e\"> small study, for example,</a> found that even moms with placental damage, presumably due to the virus, didn't transmit the virus to their infants.&#160;</p><p>While it's possible the infants in the current study contracted it after birth, there's no guarantee stricter prevention measures would have prevented it.&#160;A<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pregnant-women-coronavirus-may-pass-covid-19-in-utero-2020-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"0f02bce74059a1c076f9288b14af7dc9\">&#160;trio of studies out March 26</a> showed that some babies still tested positive for COVID-19 when strict prevention measures were taken after birth.&#160;</p><p>As the current study supports, even when infants test positive for COVID-19, they tend to fare well. A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/some-children-develop-severe-infections-from-coronavirus-2020-3?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"865c090f4c7c1a540fe4b1b18c1cec16\">study out March 17 of 2,000 kids in China who were diagnosed with</a> COVID-19, researchers found that just over 10% of all infants ended up in a severe condition.&#160;</p><p>As doctors continue to learn more about how the virus affects pregnant women and their babies, experts recommend women do what they can to manage the anxiety about the unknown.&#160;&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/coronavirus-linked-high-rates-depression-anxiety-pregnant-women-new-moms-2020-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"dabdd807c9e0ed09b16c148a32308b0a\">One report showed p</a>regnant women and new moms, who are already vulnerable to depression and anxiety, are experiencing remarkably high rates — 41% and 72% respectively — of those symptoms now.&#160;</p><p>\"There are going to be a lot of emotions, some of which are sadness, grief and the unknown,\" Dr. Jane van Dis, an OB-GYN who serves as medical director at the telemedicine network&#160;<a href=\"https://www.mavenclinic.com/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"e40ed4c31a5377b21b0cb67f70f8d4b6\">Maven</a>, previously told Business Insider. \"Just know that connecting with people who are there to support women is essential for mental health.\"&#160;</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li><strong>Read more:</strong></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-pregnant-women-should-know-about-the-coronavirus-2020-3\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">What pregnant women should know about the coronavirus</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/half-pregnant-women-in-uk-coronavirus-black-ethnic-minorities-2020-6\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">Experts are calling for an 'urgent investigation' into the high rate of pregnant women of color hospitalized with coronavirus</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pregnant-women-coronavirus-may-pass-covid-19-in-utero-2020-3\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">A trio of studies suggest pregnant women could transfer the coronavirus in utero, contradicting prior research</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/coronavirus-linked-high-rates-depression-anxiety-pregnant-women-new-moms-2020-6\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\"> Pregnant women and new moms are experiencing 'shocking' rates of anxiety and depression during the pandemic</a></li></ul><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/new-moms-covid-very-low-risk-transmission-to-babies-study-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/s-BqCQDZ2sg\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Oct 2020 15:00:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5e287127ab49fd69161f8ad3?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"db2010330ea9a30cfe1a3efe456536a7","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn23@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-54-204_dcf5916bccb750fd.webp","destWidth":4800,"destHeight":3600,"sourceBytes":1523020,"destBytes":1523020,"author":"amiller@businessinsider.com (Anna Medaris Miller)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5e1e408049878c2a2a20dad5?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn46@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-05-01-382_8fc5df633b6e2b95.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn19@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-05-00-070_60040f2d5992b97d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn63@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-59-828_0425af451c46d9dd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=s-BqCQDZ2sg:83Tl0E9VbrM:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn7@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-05-02-613_120f90ecf41f6e08.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/s-BqCQDZ2sg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn90@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-209_675820ec5676c5df.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289988},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:50","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:50","title":"America's increasingly busy bombers are sending a nuclear message to Russia and China","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/increasingly-busy-us-bombers-send-message-to-russia-and-china-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f83d9bf642e9400180b546f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force B-52 bomber\" height=\"693\" width=\"1386\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Air Force airmen prepare a US Air Force B-52H for take off during Bomber Task Force Europe 20-1, at RAF Fairford, England, October 23, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Airman 1st Class Duncan C. Bevan</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The US bomber fleet has been increasingly active, flying closer and closer to sensitive areas over Europe and the Pacific.</li>\n<li>Those flights are meant to show Moscow and Beijing what the US is capable of, but increasingly provocative flights come with higher risks, writes Michael T. Klare, professor emeritus of peace and world security studies at Hampshire College.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>On August 21, six nuclear-capable B-52H Stratofortress bombers, representing approximately <a href=\"https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/pdf/10.1080/00963402.2019.1701286\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one-seventh</a> of the war-ready US B-52H bomber fleet, <a href=\"https://www.airforcemag.com/b-52s-deploy-to-europe-train-in-norway/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flew</a> from their home base in North Dakota to Fairford Air Base in England for several weeks of intensive operations over Europe.</p><p>Although the actual weapons load of those giant bombers was kept secret, each of them is <a href=\"https://www.armscontrol.org/factsheets/unitedstatesprofile#nuclear\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">capable</a> of carrying eight <a href=\"https://missilethreat.csis.org/missile/alcm/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">AGM-86B</a> nuclear-armed, air-launched cruise missiles (ALCMs) in its bomb bay. Those six planes, in other words, could have been carrying 48 city-busting thermonuclear warheads. (The B-52H can also carry 12 ALCMs on external pylons, but none were visible on this occasion.) With such a load alone, in other words, those six planes possessed the capacity to incinerate much of western Russia, including Moscow and St. Petersburg.</p><p>The B-52 Stratofortress is no ordinary warplane. First flown in 1952, it was <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing_B-52_Stratofortress\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">designed</a> with a single purpose in mind: to cross the Atlantic or Pacific Ocean and drop dozens of nuclear bombs on the Soviet Union. Some models were later modified to deliver tons of conventional bombs on targets in North Vietnam and other hostile states, but the remaining B-52s are still largely configured for intercontinental nuclear strikes.</p><p>With only 44 of them now <a href=\"https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/pdf/10.1080/00963402.2019.1701286\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">thought</a> to be in active service at any time, those six dispatched to the edge of Russian territory represented a significant commitment of American nuclear war-making capability.</p><p>What in god's name were they doing there? According to American officials, they were intended to demonstrate this country's ability to project overwhelming power anywhere on the planet at any time and so remind our NATO allies of Washington's commitment to their defense.</p><p>\"Our ability to quickly respond and assure allies and partners rests upon the fact that we are able to deploy our B-52s at a moment's notice,\" <a href=\"https://www.usafe.af.mil/News/Press-Releases/Article/2320505/us-air-force-b-52s-return-to-europe-for-ally-partner-training/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">commented</a> Gen. Jeff Harrigian, commander of US Air Forces in Europe. \"Their presence here helps build trust with our NATO allies... and affords us new opportunities to train together through a variety of scenarios.\"</p><p>While Harrigian didn't spell out just what scenarios he had in mind, the bombers' European operations suggest that their role involved brandishing a nuclear \"stick\" in support of an increasingly hostile stance toward Russia.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5db347d8dee01903ce778096?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force B-52 bomber Baltic\" height=\"788\" width=\"1400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Air Force B-52Hs in formation during Bomber Task Force Europe 20-1, over the Baltic Sea, October 23, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Airman 1st Class Duncan C. Bevan</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>During their sojourn in Europe, for example, two of them flew over the Baltic Sea <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/davidaxe/2020/09/25/us-air-force-b-52s-just-flew-a-mock-bombing-run-on-russias-baltic-fortress/#7dbbc88779d9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">close to</a> Kaliningrad, a Russian enclave sandwiched between Poland and Lithuania that <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2018/10/17/europe/russia-kaliningrad-military-buildup-intl/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">houses</a> several key military installations. That September 25 foray coincided with a US <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-belarus-election-us-lithuania/u-s-troops-to-start-extended-exercises-in-lithuania-amid-tensions-over-belarus-idUSKBN25U1W6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">troop buildup</a> in Lithuania about 65 miles from election-embattled Belarus, a Russian neighbor.</p><p>Since August 9, when strongman Alexander Lukashenko declared victory in a presidential election <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-53721410\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">widely considered</a> fraudulent by his people and much of the international community, Belarus has experienced recurring anti-government protests.</p><p>Russian President Vladimir Putin has <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/08/27/world/europe/belarus-russia-putin.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">warned</a> that his country might intervene there if the situation \"gets out of control,\" while Secretary of State Mike Pompeo has implicitly warned of US intervention if Russia interferes. \"We stand by our long-term commitment to support Belarus' sovereignty and territorial integrity as well as the aspiration of the Belarusian people to choose their leader and to choose their own path, free from external intervention,\" he <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-belarus-election-usa-pompeo/pompeo-says-u-s-supports-international-probe-of-belarus-election-idUSKBN25G201\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">insisted</a> on August 20th.</p><p>The flight of those B-52s near Belarus can, then, be reasonably interpreted as adding a nuclear dimension to Pompeo's threat.</p><p>In another bomber deployment with no less worrisome implications, on September 4, three B-52s, accompanied by Ukrainian fighter planes, <a href=\"https://www.military.com/daily-news/2020/09/04/your-face-us-b-52s-skirt-crimea-join-ukrainian-jets-training.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flew over</a> the Black Sea near the coast of Russian-held Crimea. Like other B-52 sorties near its airspace, that foray prompted the rapid scrambling of Russian interceptor aircraft, which <a href=\"https://www.airforcetimes.com/news/your-air-force/2020/08/30/us-says-russian-military-conducted-unsafe-intercept-of-b-52-over-black-sea/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">often fly</a> threateningly close to American planes.</p><p>At a moment when tensions were <a href=\"https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/blogs/ukrainealert/vladimir-putins-hybrid-war-against-ukraine-continues/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">mounting</a> between the US-backed Ukrainian government and Russian-backed rebel areas in the eastern part of the country, the deployment of those bombers off Crimea was widely viewed as yet another nuclear-tinged threat to Moscow.</p><p>As Hans Kristensen, director of the Nuclear Information Project at the Federation of American Scientists (FAS), <a href=\"https://twitter.com/nukestrat/status/1301827862434111488\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tweeted</a>, \"Extraordinary decision to send a nuclear bomber so close to contested and tense areas. This is a real in-your-face statement.\"</p><p>And provocative as they were, those were hardly the only forays by US nuclear bombers in recent months. B-52s also ventured near Russian air space in the Arctic and within range of Russian forces in Syria. Meanwhile other B-52s, as well as nuclear-capable B-1 and B-2 bombers, have flown similar missions near Chinese positions in the South China Sea and the waters around the disputed island of Taiwan.</p><p>Never since the Cold War ended with the collapse of the Soviet Union in 1991 have so many US nuclear bombers been engaged in \"show-of-force\" operations of this sort.</p><h2>\"Demonstrating resolve\" and coercing adversaries</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5db86358dee01971713b6a12?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force B-52 bomber RAF Typhoon\" height=\"1016\" width=\"1400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A US Air Force B-52 in formation with RAF Typhoon aircraft over the North Sea, October 28, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Cpl. Alex Scott/UK Ministry of Defense</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>States have long engaged in military operations to intimidate other powers. Once upon a distant time, this would have been called \"gunboat diplomacy\" and naval vessels would have been the instruments of choice for such missions. The arrival of nuclear arms made such operations far more dangerous. This didn't, however, stop the US from <a href=\"https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/full/10.2968/062005016\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">using</a> weaponry of this sort as tools of intimidation throughout the Cold War.</p><p>In time, however, even nuclear strategists began condemning acts of \"nuclear coercion,\" arguing that such weaponry was inappropriate for any purpose other than \"deterrence\" — that is, using the threat of \"massive retaliation\" to prevent another country from attacking you. In fact, a deterrence-only posture eventually became Washington's official policy, even if the temptation to employ nukes as political cudgels <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Bomb-Presidents-Generals-History-Nuclear/dp/1982107294/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">never entirely disappeared</a> from its strategic thinking.</p><p>At a more hopeful time, President Barack Obama sought to downsize this country's nuclear arsenal and prevent the use of such weapons for anything beyond deterrence (although his administration also commenced an <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/parallels/2016/05/25/479498018/obamas-nuclear-paradox-pushing-for-cuts-agreeing-to-upgrades\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expensive \"modernization\"</a> of that arsenal).</p><p>In his widely applauded Nobel Peace Prize speech of April 5, 2009, Obama <a href=\"https://obamawhitehouse.archives.gov/the-press-office/remarks-president-barack-obama-prague-delivered\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">swore</a> to \"put an end to Cold War thinking\" and \"reduce the role of nuclear weapons in our national security strategy.\" Unfortunately, Donald Trump has sought to move the dial in the opposite direction, including increasing the use of nukes as coercive instruments.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ec433183f73707c0057e346?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force B-1B Lancer bomber Guam\" height=\"1497\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>B-1B Lancers at Andersen Air Force Base in Guam a training mission, May 14, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Senior Airman River Bruce</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The president's deep desire to bolster the role of nuclear weapons in national security was first spelled out in his administration's <a href=\"https://media.defense.gov/2018/Feb/02/2001872886/-1/-1/1/2018-NUCLEAR-POSTURE-REVIEW-FINAL-REPORT.PDF\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nuclear Posture Review</a> of February 2018. In addition to calling for the accelerated modernization of the nuclear arsenal, it also endorsed the use of such weapons to demonstrate American \"resolve\" — in other words, a willingness to go to the nuclear brink over political differences.</p><p>A large and diverse arsenal was desirable, the document noted, to \"demonstrate resolve through the positioning of forces, messaging, and flexible response options.\" Nuclear bombers were said to be especially useful for such a purpose: \"Flights abroad,\" it stated, \"display US capabilities and resolve, providing effective signaling for deterrence and assurance, including in times of tension.\"</p><p>Ever since, the Trump administration has been deploying the country's nuclear bomber fleet of B-52s, B-1s, and B-2s with increasing frequency to \"display US capabilities and resolve,\" particularly with respect to Russia and China.</p><p>The supersonic <a href=\"https://www.military.com/equipment/b-1b-lancer\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">B-1B Lancer</a>, developed in the 1970s, was originally meant to replace the B-52 as the nation's premier long-range nuclear bomber. After the Cold War ended, however, it was converted to carry conventional munitions and is no longer officially designated as a nuclear delivery system — though it could be reconfigured for this purpose at any time.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.military.com/equipment/b-2-spirit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">B-2 Spirit</a>, with its distinctive flying-wing design, was the first US bomber built with \"stealth\" capabilities (meant to avoid detection by enemy radar systems) and is configured to carry both nuclear and conventional weaponry. For the past year or so, those two planes plus the long-lived B-52 have been used on an almost weekly basis as the radioactive \"stick\" of US diplomacy around the world.</p><h2>Nuclear forays in the Arctic and the Russian Far East</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4a9bdb7ffa48002894d077?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Norway F-16 Air Force B-52\" height=\"675\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Norwegian F-16 fighter jets train with US Air Force B-52 bombers, August 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Norwegian Armed Forces</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>When flying to Europe in August, those six B-52s from North Dakota's Minot Air Force Base took a <a href=\"https://www.thedrive.com/the-war-zone/35962/six-b-52-strategic-bombers-fly-alongside-norwegian-fighters-in-clear-signal-to-russia\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">roundabout route</a> north of Greenland (which President Trump had <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/07/22/politics/trump-buy-greenland-pompeo/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">unsuccessfully offered</a> to purchase in 2019). They finally descended over the Barents Sea within easy missile-firing range of Russia's <a href=\"https://www.csis.org/features/ice-curtain-russias-arctic-military-presence\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">vast naval complex</a> at Murmansk, the home for most of its ballistic missile submarines.</p><p>For Hans Kristensen of FAS, that was <a href=\"https://twitter.com/nukestrat/status/1297538866589642752\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">another</a> obvious and \"pointed message at Russia.\"</p><p>Strategically speaking, Washington had largely ignored the Arctic until a combination of factors — global warming, accelerated oil and gas drilling in the region, and increased Russian and Chinese military activities there — sparked growing interest.</p><p>As global temperatures have risen, the Arctic ice cap has been melting at an ever-faster pace, allowing energy firms to exploit the region's <a href=\"https://pubs.usgs.gov/fs/2008/3049/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">extensive hydrocarbon resources</a>. This, in turn, has led to <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Race-Whats-Left-Scramble-Resources/dp/0805091262/'\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">feverish efforts</a> by the region's littoral states, led by Russia, to lay claim to such resources and build up their military capabilities there.</p><p>In light of these developments, the Trump administration, led by Secretary of State Mike Pompeo, has <a href=\"https://www.tomdispatch.com/post/176603/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">called for</a> an expansion of this country's Arctic military forces.</p><p>In a speech delivered at the Arctic Council in Rovaniemi, Finland, in May 2019, Pompeo warned of Russia's growing military stance in the region and pledged a strong American response to it. \"Under President Trump,\" he <a href=\"https://www.state.gov/looking-north-sharpening-americas-arctic-focus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">declared</a>. \"We are fortifying America's security and diplomatic presence in the area.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5db736b4dee0192b74578808?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force B-1B bomber F-22 EA-18G\" height=\"798\" width=\"1199\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Air Force B-1B bombers escorted by an F-22 and two EA-18Gs over the Persian Gulf, October 24, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In line with this, the Pentagon has deployed US warships to the Arctic on a regular basis, while engaging in ever more elaborate military exercises there.</p><p>These have included <a href=\"https://www.tomdispatch.com/blog/176661/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cold Response 2020</a>, conducted this spring in Norway's far north within a few hundred miles of those key Russian bases at Murmansk. For the most part, however, the administration has relied on nuclear-bomber forays to demonstrate its opposition to an increasing Russian role there.</p><p>In November 2019, for example, three B-52s, accompanied by Norwegian F-16 fighter jets, <a href=\"https://thebarentsobserver.com/en/security/2019/11/us-b-52-strategic-bombers-and-norwegian-f-16s-flying-wing-wing-over-barents-sea\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">approached</a> the Russian naval complex at Murmansk, a move meant to demonstrate the Pentagon's capacity to launch nuclear-armed missiles at one of that country's most critical military installations.</p><p>If the majority of such nuclear forays have occurred near Norway's far north, the Pentagon has not neglected Russia's far eastern territory, home of its Pacific Fleet, either.</p><p>In an unusually brazen maneuver, this May a B-1B bomber <a href=\"https://www.thedrive.com/the-war-zone/33637/b-1b-bomber-made-bold-flight-into-the-sea-of-okhotsk-that-is-surrounded-by-russian-territory\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flew over</a> the Sea of Okhotsk, an offshoot of the Pacific Ocean surrounded by Russian territory on three sides (Siberia to the north, Sakhalin Island to the west, and the Kamchatka Peninsula to the east).</p><p>As if to add insult to injury, the Air Force dispatched two B-52H bombers over the Sea of Okhotsk in June — another first for an aircraft of that type. Needless to say, incursions in such a militarily sensitive area led to the <a href=\"https://www.thedrive.com/the-war-zone/34220/russia-sent-three-types-of-fighters-to-intercept-b-52s-flying-rare-mission-into-sea-of-okhotsk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">rapid scrambling</a> of Russian fighter aircraft.</p><h2>The South China Sea and Taiwan</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/59fcc81413ed5103215e7ea7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"B-1B Lancer\" height=\"986\" width=\"1440\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A B-1B takes off from Andersen Air Force Base in Guam, October 11, 2017.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>A similar, equally provocative pattern can be observed in the East and South China Seas. Even as President Trump has sought, largely unsuccessfully, to negotiate a trade deal with Beijing, his administration has become increasingly antagonistic toward the Chinese leadership.</p><p>On July 23, Secretary of State Pompeo delivered a particularly hostile <a href=\"https://www.state.gov/communist-china-and-the-free-worlds-future/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">speech</a> in the presidential library of Richard Nixon, the very commander-in-chief who first reopened relations with communist China. Pompeo called on American allies to suspend normal relations with Beijing and, like Washington, treat it as a hostile power, much the way the Soviet Union was viewed during the Cold War.</p><p>While administration rhetoric amped up, the Department of Defense has been bolstering its capacity to engage and defeat Beijing in any future conflict. In its 2018 <a href=\"https://dod.defense.gov/Portals/1/Documents/pubs/2018-National-Defense-Strategy-Summary.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">National Defense Strategy</a>, as the US military's \"forever wars\" dragged on, the Pentagon suddenly labeled China and Russia the two greatest threats to American security.</p><p>More recently, it singled out China alone as the overarching menace to American national security. \"In this era of great-power competition,\" Secretary of Defense Mark Esper <a href=\"https://www.defense.gov/Newsroom/Speeches/Speech/Article/2350362/secretary-of-defense-speech-at-rand-as-delivered/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">declared</a> this September, \"the Department of Defense has prioritized China, then Russia, as our top strategic competitors.\"</p><p>The Pentagon's efforts have largely been focused on the South China Sea, where China has established a network of small military installations on artificial islands created by dredging sand from the sea-bottom near some of the reefs and atolls it claims.</p><p>American leaders have never accepted the legitimacy of this island-building project and have repeatedly called upon Beijing to dismantle the bases. Such efforts have, however, largely fallen on deaf ears and it's now evident that the Pentagon is considering military means to eliminate the island threat.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5efc9da63f73702fd041929d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Paratroopers descend on Andersen Air Force Base in Guam\" height=\"668\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Paratroopers descend on Andersen Air Force Base in Guam.\n<p class=\"copyright\">U.S. Air Force photo by Staff Sgt. Divine Cox</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In early July, the US Navy conducted its most elaborate maneuvers to date in those waters, <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-shows-off-its-firepower-to-beijing-in-south-china-sea-11593965632\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">deploying</a> two aircraft carriers there — the USS Nimitz and the USS Ronald Reagan — plus an escort fleet of cruisers, destroyers, and submarines. While there, the two carriers launched hundreds of combat planes in simulated attacks on military bases on the islands the Chinese had essentially built.</p><p>At the same time, paratroopers from the Army's 25th Infantry Division were <a href=\"https://www.armytimes.com/news/your-army/2020/07/01/paratroopers-flew-from-alaska-to-practice-seizing-a-pacific-air-base/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flown</a> from their home base in Alaska to the Pacific island of Guam in what was clearly meant as a simulated air assault on a (presumably Chinese) military installation. And just to make sure the leadership in Beijing understood that, in any actual encounter with US forces, Chinese resistance would be countered by the maximum level of force deemed necessary, the Pentagon <a href=\"https://www.navytimes.com/news/your-navy/2020/07/06/two-us-aircraft-carriers-are-operating-in-the-south-china-sea-air-force-b-52-joins-them/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">also flew</a> a B-52 bomber over those carriers as they engaged in their provocative maneuvers.</p><p>And that was hardly the first visit of a nuclear bomber to the South China Sea. The Pentagon has, in fact, been deploying such planes there on a regular basis since the beginning of 2020.</p><p>In April, for example, the Air Force <a href=\"https://theaviationist.com/2020/04/30/u-s-b-1-bombers-conduct-32-hour-round-trip-mission-to-south-china-sea-to-demonstrate-global-reach/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">dispatched</a> two B-1B Lancers on a 32-hour round-trip from their home at Ellsworth Air Force Base, North Dakota, to that sea and back as a demonstration of its ability to project power even in the midst of the pandemic President Trump likes to <a href=\"https://www.concordmonitor.com/First-presidential-debate-Trump-Biden-full-transcript-36532544\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">call</a> \"the Chinese plague.\"</p><p>Meanwhile, tensions have grown over the status of the island of Taiwan, which China views as a breakaway part of the country. Beijing has been pressuring its leaders to foreswear any moves toward independence, while the Trump administration tacitly endorses just such a future by doing the previously unimaginable — notably, by <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/17/world/asia/us-official-taiwan-china.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">sending</a> high-level officials, Secretary of Health and Human Services Alex Azar among them, on visits to the island and by promising deliveries of increasingly sophisticated weapons.</p><p>Meanwhile, the Pentagon has upped its military presence in that part of the Pacific, too. The Navy has repeatedly <a href=\"https://news.usni.org/2020/08/31/u-s-destroyer-transits-taiwan-strait-for-second-time-in-august\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">dispatched</a> missile-armed destroyers on \"freedom of navigation\" missions through the Taiwan Strait, while other US warships have conducted elaborate military exercises in nearby waters.</p><p>Needless to say, such provocative steps have alarmed Beijing, which has responded by <a href=\"https://www.voanews.com/east-asia-pacific/increased-china-warplane-activity-unnerves-taiwan\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">increasing</a> the incursions of its military aircraft into airspace claimed by Taiwan.</p><p>To make sure that Beijing fully appreciates the depth of American \"resolve\" to resist any attempt to seize Taiwan by force, the Pentagon has accompanied its other military moves around the island with — you guessed it — <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-taiwan-china-usa/taiwan-says-u-s-flies-bombers-near-island-after-chinas-drills-idUSKBN2060UO\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flights</a> of B-52 bombers.</p><h2>Playing with Fire</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5c40d5cfd118933c60724592?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A B-2 Spirit bomber deployed from Whiteman Air Force Base, Missouri, and F-22 Raptors from the Hawaii Air National Guard’s 154th Wing fly near Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam, Hawaii, during an interoperability training mission Jan. 15, 2019.\" height=\"666\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A B-2 Spirit bomber and F-22 Raptors on a training flight near Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam in Hawaii, January 15, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">U.S. Air Force photo by Master Sgt. Russ Scalf</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>And where will all this end? As the US sends nuclear-capable bombers on increasingly provocative flights ever closer to Russian and Chinese territory, the danger of an accident or mishap is bound to grow.</p><p>Sooner or later, a fighter plane from one of those countries is going to get too close to an American bomber and a deadly incident will occur. And what will happen if a nuclear bomber, armed with advanced missiles and electronics (even conceivably nuclear weapons), is in some fashion downed?</p><p>Count on one thing: In Donald Trump's America, the calls for devastating retaliation will be intense and a major conflagration cannot be ruled out.</p><p>Bluntly put, dispatching nuclear-capable B-52s on simulated bombing runs against Chinese and Russian military installations is simply nuts. Yes, it must scare the bejesus out of Chinese and Russian officials, but it will also prompt them to distrust any future peaceful overtures from American diplomats while further bolstering their own military power and defenses.</p><p>Eventually, we will all find ourselves in an ever more dangerous and insecure world with the risk of Armageddon lurking just around the corner.</p><p><em>Michael T. Klare, a <a href=\"https://www.tomdispatch.com/blog/176745/tomgram%3A_michael_klare%2C_artificial_%28un%29intelligence_and_the_u.s._military\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TomDispatch regular</a>, is the five-college professor emeritus of peace and world security studies at Hampshire College and a senior visiting fellow at the Arms Control Association. He is the author of 15 books, the latest of which is <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/1627792481/ref=nosim/?tag=tomdispatch-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">All Hell Breaking Loose: The Pentagon's Perspective on Climate Change</a>.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
