//cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=2DiM1KDFiGM:O3gi4UNLiQI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn95@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-05-00-879_f4b9c9e9007293b5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/2DiM1KDFiGM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn91@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-52-666_7eebd8bab77265a7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522290011},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:50","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:50","title":"From pay cuts to permanent work-from-home, here's how Silicon Valley companies are thinking about the future of work","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/silicon-valley-future-of-work-port-coronavirus-apple-amazon-facebook-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f80c3324c3b2e0019bba47b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Facebook headquarters campus sign employee\" height=\"2378\" width=\"3171\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">JOSH EDELSON/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The world's biggest tech companies have varying plans for the future of work.&#160;</li>\n<li>Some companies, like Twitter and Slack, have said employees never need to return to the office.</li>\n<li>Others, like Microsoft, are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/microsoft-employess-to-work-from-home-permanently-2020-10\">reportedly adopting a hybrid model</a> where employees report to the office only a few days per week.&#160;</li>\n<li>Companies like Amazon and Salesforce are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/silicon-valley-parenting-perks-benefits-coronavirus-pandemic-google-facebook-amazon-2020-10\">adopting new benefits to help out working parents</a>, like subsidized back-up childcare and extended paid leave.</li>\n<li>At Facebook, employees may work from home permanently, but if they leave the Bay Area for a less expensive city, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/21/technology/facebook-remote-work-coronavirus.html\">they'll likely face a pay cut</a> starting in January.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The future of Silicon Valley may bear little resemblance to the thriving hub we knew before the pandemic.&#160;</p><p>Since the coronavirus pandemic hit the US in March, tech companies based in San Francisco Bay Area have largely shut down their sprawling campuses and asked employees to work from home — in some cases, forever.</p><p>Eventually, whether it's in January, next summer, or beyond, those offices will reopen their doors, but office life is unlikely to resemble the before times for the workers who choose to return.&#160;</p><p>For some companies, that may mean a rethink to their physical spaces in order to prevent the spread of disease. For others, it may mean changing their real estate plans altogether, opting instead for a new type of office, or none at all. In some cases, it may mean rethinking where employees live and how they're paid.&#160;</p><p>Here's how tech's biggest companies are planning for the future of work.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tTwitter was already preparing for a \"decentralized\" workforce, even before the pandemic.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc2a5c4049200115cb6b2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"twitter HQ san francisco\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Twitter&#39;s headquarters in San Francisco.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Justin Sullivan/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>While Twitter employees were told earlier this year that they have the option of working from home on a permanent basis, a decentralized workforce has been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-employees-working-from-home-resources-tools-2020-10\">a dream of CEO Jack Dorsey's for a few years</a>.&#160;&#160;</p><p>As a result, Twitter may have a clearer picture than most of its future plans. The company already had plans in place for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-companies-cutting-salaries-outside-bay-area-twitter-facebook-vmware-2020-9\">localizing pay based on where employees choose to live</a> and has started <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-subleasing-san-francisco-headquarters-employees-work-from-home-2020-9\">subleasing office space</a> in San Francisco &#8212; 100,000 square feet, to be exact.</p><p>Even before the pandemic hit the Bay Area, some managers at Twitter had started experimenting with working from home and testing virtual meetings, according to <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2020/10/01/twitter-work-from-home/?arc404=true\">a recent report from the Washington Post</a>.&#160;</p><p>Elsewhere at Twitter, teams working to make video meetings more seamless, like using hand signals for when they have something to say or need to sign off, and inventing new phrases like \"ELMO\" &#8212; short for \"Enough! Let's move on\" &#8212; to help get meetings back on track, according to the Post.&#160;</p>\n\tGoogle isn't requiring employees to return to the office until July 2021.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc1c80f4d5500110321c3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mask google\" height=\"2972\" width=\"3963\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Google&#39;s offices in the Chelsea neighborhood of New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Noam Galai/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Google confirmed in July that its employees wouldn't be required to come back to the office <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-employees-working-from-home-summer-2021-report-2020-7\">until next summer</a>, partly to help workers with school-aged children who may not be returning to in-person schooling.&#160;</p><p>The company has made other changes to help out working parents, most notably by adding eight extra weeks to its Carers leave policy: Google employees now get 14 weeks total, which can be broken up hourly.&#160;</p><p>In addition, Google offered its employees $1,000 allowances to help them set up home offices.&#160;</p><p>During an all-hands on October 1, Google CEO Sundar Pichai said the company is planning on adding more hub offices, which will give employees more choice in where they live, according to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-ceo-elaborates-future-office-plans-as-employees-demand-answers-2020-10\">leaked audio obtained by Business Insider's Hugh Langley</a>.</p><p>While Pichai said he believes most roles at Google should include office work, he described a model of \"hybrid-flexible work,\" which would presumably allow employees to keep working from home some of the time.&#160;</p>\n\tFacebook has given employees $2,000 in bonuses to help them set up home offices.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc5a10f4d5500110321d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Facebook headquarters\" height=\"1934\" width=\"2583\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Facebook&#39;s headquarters in Menlo Park, California.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jeff Chiu/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Facebook has said that employees may continue working remotely through June 2021, but many may choose to do so on a permanent basis &#8212; they will, however, likely take a pay cut beginning in January if they choose to move to a less expensive region than the Bay Area, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/21/technology/facebook-remote-work-coronavirus.html\">according to The New York Times</a>.</p><p>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/21/technology/facebook-remote-work-coronavirus.html\">said in May</a> that he expects 50% of the company's workforce to be entirely remote within the next decade.</p><p>Given that employees won't be returning to Facebook's Menlo Park headquarters anytime soon, the company has shifted some of its on-campus employee perks to accommodate working from home. The company said in August that it was giving employees an additional $1,000 stipend for setting up a home office, on top of the $1,000 working-from-home bonus <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-gives-employees-1000-dollar-bonus-coronavirus-2020-3\">they were given in March</a>.&#160;</p><p>Facebook is also making plans to help out working parents, including offering 10 weeks of paid leave for employees who unexpectedly need to care for a child or relative.</p><p>Additionally, Facebook plans to give all employees high marks on their performance reviews in 2020, which typically results in bonuses, <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/business/technology/story/2020-03-31/coronavirus-google-facebook-paid-leave-school-closures\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\">according to the Los Angeles Times.</a></p>\n\tAmazon has started offering generous benefits to parents.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc241c4049200115cb6b1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Amazon Seattle headquarters\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Amazon&#39;s headquarters in Seattle.\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Moore/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Amazon announced in July that it would allow employees to continue working remotely until January 8, 2021, as long as their jobs can be effectively done from home.&#160;</p><p>For those employees who do choose to come into the office, however, Amazon has implemented safety procedures like physical distancing, increased cleaning, and temperature checks, and the company provides face coverings and hand sanitizer, a spokesperson <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-employees-work-from-home-until-next-year-covid-19-2020-7\">told Business Insider in July</a>.&#160;</p><p>In response to pandemic, Amazon has also implemented new employee benefits. The company has begun offering discounts on tutoring, as well as subsidizing backup childcare for up to 10 days a month for full- and part-time Amazon and Whole Foods employees &#8212; Amazon says it covers more than 90% of the cost.&#160;</p><p>But while many tech companies appear to be rethinking the future of physical offices, Amazon has continued its expansion plans &#8212; but not at its Seattle headquarters. The company recently announced&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-adds-jobs-new-office-hub-locations-2020-8\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\">a $1.4 billion investment</a> to expand its physical offices in six US cities and hire 3,500 new employees who will report into those hubs.</p>\n\tSalesforce is letting employees work from home until August 2021.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc5220f4d5500110321d6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Salesforce Tower\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Salesforce Tower in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brendan McDermid/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Earlier this year, Salesforce wrote a 21-page handbook, available to anyone who wants it, about how to safely reopen office spaces. The plan includes rethinking some of the materials inside the office, adding glass dividers, and mandating social distancing, even in elevators.&#160;</p><p>While Salesforce is reopening some offices in places like Canada, Europe, and Asia, all of its employees may continue working from home until August 2021.</p><p>Salesforce has also adopted new benefits for parents during the pandemic. The company <a href=\"https://www.salesforce.com/news/stories/deepening-support-for-employees-with-expanded-benefits/\">announced in August</a> that parents are now eligible for up to six weeks off and that Salesforce will also offer subsidized back-up childcare: employees may get reimbursed up to $100 per day for 5 days every month through January 2021.&#160;</p>\n\tSlack employees can work remotely on a permanent basis if they'd like.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6a488f49479600287bd923?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Slack headquarters\" height=\"1735\" width=\"2314\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Justin Sullivan/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://slack.com/blog/news/june-update-on-slack-office-closures-from-slack-svp-of-people-robby-kwok\">Slack announced in June</a> that it would allow its employees the option to work remotely forever, and said it plans to hire more workers who will be permanently remote.&#160;</p><p>Slack also pushed its office reopening date, saying it expects the office will look \"quite different\" going forward: \"fewer amenities such as catered lunches and coffee bars, less focus on in-person meetings with colleagues, and more options for focused solo work.\"</p>\n\tApple CEO Tim Cook has said that after the pandemic, the company will not \"return to the way we were.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc3030f4d5500110321c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"apple park\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The visitor&#39;s center at Apple&#39;s headquarters in Cupertino, California.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Eric Risberg/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>While some Apple employees have been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-return-to-work-plan-vs-google-microsoft-silicon-valley-2020-5\">reporting to the company's offices for months</a>, others have worked remotely &#8212; and Apple CEO Tim Cook said recently that it's been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-ceo-tim-cook-predicts-remote-work-habits-remain-forever-2020-9\">a successful experiment for the company.</a></p><p>\"There are some things that actually work really well virtually,\" Cook said in an interview at <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y06UTlSn2hw\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\">The Atlantic Festival</a> last month, but that working remotely is \"not like being together physically.\"</p><p>In <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-07-30/apple-kicks-u-s-office-return-back-to-early-2021-ceo-cook-says?sref=nOLch4DD\">an interview with Bloomberg</a> in July, Cook said Apple employees can continue working from home until early 2021. \"To go beyond that, it would depend on the success with a vaccine, success with therapeutics,\" and other factors, Cook told Bloomberg.&#160;</p><p>Apple's offices will function like an accordion, he told Bloomberg, allowing them to open and close depending on data surrounding virus cases.&#160;</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tMicrosoft will reportedly allow its 150,000-person workforce to work from home at least part of the time.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc33ec4049200115cb6b8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Microsoft headquarters in Redmond, Washington.\" height=\"3053\" width=\"4071\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Microsoft&#39;s headquarters in Redmond, Washington.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Stephen Brashear</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In what Microsoft is calling a \"hybrid workplace,\" employees will now only have to report to the office for half the workweek, according to <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/10/9/21508964/microsoft-remote-work-from-home-covid-19-coronavirus\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\">an internal memo obtained by The Verge this month.</a> If approved by a manager, some employees will be allowed to work from home permanently and relocate, but if they do, they'll need to give up their work station at Microsoft's office.</p><p>However, some employees won't have the option of remote work, The Verge reports. If an employee works in Microsoft's hardware division or in-person training, they'll need to report to the office.&#160;</p>\n\tNetflix CEO Reed Hastings says the company's offices won't reopen until the majority of people are vaccinated.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6cc4800f4d5500110321cf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Netflix headquarters\" height=\"1996\" width=\"2662\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Netflix&#39;s headquarters in Los Angeles.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chris Pizzello/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In a new interview with&#160;<a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/netflixs-reed-hastings-deems-remote-work-a-pure-negative-11599487219?mod=djemalertNEWS\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"ed899db228341e59f80ab2079d462472\">The Wall Street Journal</a> last month, Hastings said he hasn't seen any upsides of remote work.&#160;</p><p>\"No. I don't see any positives,\" Hastings told the Journal. \"Not being able to get together in person, particularly internationally, is a pure negative. I've been super impressed at people's sacrifices.\"</p><p>Hastings said employees <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/netflix-office-reopening-employees-coronavirus-covid-vaccine-reed-hastings-2020-9\">won't return to the office until there's a vaccine</a>, however &#8212; likely six months after a vaccine is widely available, or once there are \"a majority of people vaccinated.\"</p><p>In the future, Hastings expects the corporate world to shift to a four-day workweek where employees report to the office for four days and work remotely on the fifth.&#160;</p>\n\tStripe is cutting pay for employees who relocate, but will also provide one-time bonuses.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8464c3642e9400180b551a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"john collison getty Handout\" height=\"799\" width=\"1065\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Stripe cofounder John Collison.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.gettyimages.co.uk/license/458458278\" target=\"_blank\">Getty/Handout</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>For Stripe employees based in major cities, the company has started offering a new deal: move out of New York, Seattle, or the Bay Area and take a pay cut &#8212; but also receive a $20,000 bonus, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-09-15/stripe-employees-who-relocate-to-get-20-000-bonus-and-a-pay-cut\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\">a Bloomberg report from last month.</a></p><p>Stripe employees may see as much as a 10% cut to their base salary for relocating. The offer will be available to anyone who decides to move before the end of 2020, Bloomberg reports.&#160;</p>\n\tSoftware company VMware has said employees may work remotely forever, but may take a pay cut.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f846754642e9400180b5527?format=jpeg\" alt=\"VMware headquarters\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2223\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Yichuan Cao/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>VMware told its employees earlier this year that they may work remotely on a permanent basis.</p><p>But recently, it decided to reduce the salaries of those who have moved to less expensive cities, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-09-11/vmware-twitter-cut-pay-for-remote-workers-fleeing-bay-area?sref=BWbpWjRm\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\">a recent Bloomberg report</a>. Medical marijuana is legal in 33 states, meaning that a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/legal-marijuana-states-2018-1\">majority of Americans now have some form of access to legal marijuana</a>.</p><p>Ballot initiatives like the ones voters are considering on November 3 have played a major role in the spread of legal cannabis. Nine of the states that legalized recreational marijuana did so through referendums.</p><p>Business Insider put together a <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f62024c323fc4001e0d6862?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Boris Johnson\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>UK Prime Minister Boris Johnson.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>UK Prime Minister Boris Johnson on Monday announced details of a new three-tier system for local lockdowns in England.</li>\n<li>Areas in the most serious tier, \"very high,\" will be required to ban household mixing, advise people not to travel outside the area, and close pubs and bars &#8212; though pubs will be allowed to stay open if they can operate as restaurants.</li>\n<li>Areas in the second tier, \"high,\" will also ban household mixing indoors.</li>\n<li>Areas in the least serious tier, \"medium,\" will continue with national social-distancing rules, the \"rule of six,\" and the 10 p.m. hospitality curfew.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Households will be barred from mixing indoors and pubs and bars will be closed from Wednesday in large parts of England under a new system for local lockdowns.</p><p>UK Prime Minister Boris Johnson on Monday afternoon unveiled details of the new \"local COVID alert levels,\" under which areas of England will be put into one of three categories — \"medium,\" \"high,\" and \"very high\" — depending on their rates of coronavirus infections and hospitalizations.</p><p>Johnson told members of Parliament that he took \"no pleasure\" in announcing the restrictions but insisted that \"we must act to save lives.\"</p><p>Areas in the \"very high\" tier will have the strictest rules. Household mixing will be banned, and people will be advised not to travel outside their area except for essential reasons like for work or health. Pubs and bars will be closed, though pubs that can operate as restaurants <a href=\"https://london.eater.com/2020/10/12/21512742/uk-coronavirus-restriction-tiers-medium-risk-high-risk-very-high-risk-boris-johnson\">will be allowed to stay open</a> as long as they serve alcohol only with meals.</p><p>\"In these areas the government will set a baseline of prohibiting social mixing indoors and in private gardens and, I'm sorry to say, closing pubs and bars,\" Johnson told MPs.</p><p>Schools, universities, and stores will remain open, however.</p><p>Areas in the \"high\" tier will ban household mixing indoors, while those in the \"medium\" tier will be asked only to follow the current national rules such as wearing face masks, observing <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/news/rule-of-six-comes-into-effect-to-tackle-coronavirus\">the \"rule of six,\"</a> and following the 10 p.m. curfew for hospitality settings.</p><p>Areas already under local restrictions will automatically go into the \"high\" level, Johnson said.</p><p>The restrictions are designed to be a baseline, and local authorities will be allowed to impose further restrictions if necessary, Johnson said.</p><p>The UK government is expected to reveal a full list of areas and their tiers later on Monday.</p><p>The prime minister is also expected to explain the new system to the public in a televised press conference on Monday evening alongside his scientific advisors and Chancellor Rishi Sunak.</p><p>Johnson's opponents accused him of losing control of the outbreak.</p><p>\"I am now deeply sceptical whether the government has got a plan to gain control of this virus,\" said Keir Starmer, the Labour Party leader.</p><p>\"We tried to give the prime minister the benefit of the doubt, but it increasingly feels like the Prime Minister is several steps behind the curve and running to catch up with the virus that he has lost control of long ago.\"</p><p>Andy Street, the Conservative mayor for the West Midlands, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/andy4wm/status/1315671062802243586\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said he was \"disappointed\"</a> by the UK government's decision to put the region in the \"high\" tier and urged it to \"review this decision as soon as possible.\" He added that restricting hospitality businesses \"will not solve\" the region's \"main problem\" of virus transmission in households.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\" /></a> \n</div>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/QWHvJoG_uPk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" />","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Oct 2020 14:55:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5efccfc85af6cc158d3bb219?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"fb8b4cd68264559b74516615ed1bfa89","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn6@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-54-110_6a488e2a59f76284.webp","destWidth":1879,"destHeight":1410,"sourceBytes":77952,"destBytes":77952,"author":"insider@insider.com (Business Insider)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f5007eae6ff30001d4e6c01?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn97@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-56-809_fb4fd68fc2f1cb2f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=QWHvJoG_uPk:Ip8dVRldqhU:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn76@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-05-03-119_342307cd89c12409.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=QWHvJoG_uPk:Ip8dVRldqhU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn16@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-59-362_3326bdd059b913b0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=QWHvJoG_uPk:Ip8dVRldqhU:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn70@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-505_947ba7b7227f1993.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/QWHvJoG_uPk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn62@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-02-249_19d3be2b83bca6b8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289886},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"I'm the CEO of an 100-person agency. Here's how I designed my office to work better and avoid distractions.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/ceo-took-an-engineers-approach-designing-home-office-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f721c2774fe5b0018a8dc88?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Image (1)\" height=\"768\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ben Crudo&#39;s home office.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ben Crudo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://twitter.com/bengmn\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"ae4c63fe0f743c62819aaa5e0ed970b7\">Ben Crudo</a>&#160;is CEO of&#160;<a href=\"https://www.diffagency.com/?utm_medium=pr&utm_source=csuite&utm_campaign=benpublicationsications\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"5916025d94fe0bc57a92c108cf245188\">Diff Agency</a>&#160;and&#160;an ecommerce expert helping retailers win today and tomorrow.</li>\n<li>Six months in, it's clear that we're not returning to the office anytime soon &#8212; and that means it's time to create a more intentional work from home space.</li>\n<li>Crudo says it's worth investing in things you thing really need, including things that make you feel comfortable (like a good office chair).</li>\n<li>You need to insulate from your distraction, both in your physical space and in how you spend your time and energy.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>So, tough love: Like it or not, we're not all going back to the office anytime soon. Six months into the pandemic, if you haven't set up a proper home office yet, it's time to step away from the kitchen table and create a real, dedicated work space.&#160;&#160;&#160;</p><p>The number one priority — from my lens as an engineer and the CEO of a <a href=\"https://www.diffagency.com/\">100-plus person agency</a> — has to be <em>intentionality</em>. Being deliberate about the office you set up is critical. In fact, the opportunity to do this is one of the unexpected boons of this entire work-from-home experience. The fact is the traditional<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/brit-morse/remote-work-survey-owl-labs.html\"> office environment — from 9-5 to cubicles to dress codes — didn't work for everyone</a>. If there's one unexpected benefit of the massive shift to work from home, it's that it has given us a unique chance to personalize how, where and even when we work.&#160;</p><p>At home, we're free to tailor our space to what suits us and our needs. Here's a glimpse into my own set-up — not as a model to emulate, but as an example of what personalization and being deliberate can look like in practice.&#160;&#160;</p><h2><strong>Invest in stuff you really need — and stuff that makes you really comfortable</strong></h2><p>As an engineer, I try to be pragmatic: You don't need the latest tech toy, but quality tools you really like will keep you dialed in. I've learned that simplicity goes a long way when paired with a few luxurious touches.&#160;</p><p>Obvious one here, but an ergonomic chair might be the best investment you'll make. It will make your workday easier on your body and you'll be able to sustain longer work sessions and feel happier doing it. (At my company, we've provided <a href=\"https://www.humanscale.com/products/seating\">Humanscale ergonomic chairs</a> to all employees for exactly this reason.)</p><p>That low-res monitor? It's a waste of desk space. Cycling through windows (or worse, relying on multiple monitors) is unproductive and frustrating. With a high res monitor, I find that I don't have to split my attention as much. Even stuff like the right mouse and keyboard matter. I have an <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/shop/product/MLA22LL/A/magic-keyboard-us-english\">Apple Magic Keyboard</a> that is light, wireless and portable so I can switch up my setting when I need a change of scenery.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Building a great home office doesn't mean you have to spend a lot on gear. In fact, some of the things that make me happiest working from home are low-cost, but intentional, touches. My leather keyboard pad and mouse pad are small things, but whenever my hands hit the surface in front of me, it's a grounding reminder of where I am. I also have a <a href=\"https://www.yeti.com/en_CA/drinkware/rambler-414-ml-mug/70000000335.html#start=1\">Yeti coffee mug</a> that keeps my coffee warm for hours.&#160;</p><p>And let's not forget about art — <em>your art</em>, not some generic office art. I've got an art deco take on Sunset Strip on my wall that's a family heirloom. Contemplating art that moves you can actually help your focus, make you<a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2020/01/11/795010044/feeling-artsy-heres-how-making-art-helps-your-brain\"> more hopeful</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.inverse.com/mind-body/abstract-art-mindset-study\">improve your decision making</a>.&#160;&#160;</p><h2><strong>Outsmarting distraction</strong></h2><p>Whatever gear or decor you choose, your home office will fall short without one additional step: insulating yourself from distraction.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Before the pandemic struck, employees were<a href=\"https://hbr.org/2020/06/a-plan-for-managing-constant-interruptions-at-work\"> interrupted every six to 12 minutes</a>. Now, it's got to be far worse, between juggling personal and work lives under the same roof, yet another Zoom meeting, and constant coronavirus updates. For all these reasons, building and sustaining focus is one of the most important parts of remote work.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Step one: turn your notifications off. You don't have to go so far as giving up your smartphone<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-ceo-give-up-smartphone-dumb-phone-better-leader-2019-11#limited-contact-equals-better-leadership-2\"> like I did</a>, but be disciplined about giving your<a href=\"https://health.clevelandclinic.org/science-clear-multitasking-doesnt-work/\"> undivided attention to the task at hand</a>. Quick hack: I've started using a <a href=\"https://bulletjournal.com/\">bullet journal</a> instead of relying on digital schedulers or to-do lists. When I think of something I need to come back to, or an item for my to-do list, I jot it down by hand. An analog notebook <a href=\"https://www.fastcompany.com/90469534/how-to-use-a-bullet-journal-to-kickstart-your-mindfulness-practice\">keeps me mindful</a> without derailing my focus.&#160;</p><p>I've even found that it's important to be more intentional with my media consumption so I don't get overwhelmed by all the bad news. In the early days of quarantine it was easy to <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/worklife/article/20200505-coronavirus-how-much-news-is-too-much\">fall prey to information overload</a>. Forty-three percent of Americans say the news makes them <a href=\"https://www.journalism.org/2020/04/29/about-seven-in-ten-u-s-adults-say-they-need-to-take-breaks-from-covid-19-news/\">feel emotionally worse</a> and I can relate. Particularly in a time of crisis, it's important to guard your mental space. Now I spend 10 to 20 minutes cycling through news from a few different trusted sources every couple of days. I focus on what I'm interested in and that's it — no more mindless <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/petersuciu/2020/09/22/doomscrolling-isnt-helping-our-well-being-warn-experts/\">doom scrolling</a>.&#160;</p><p>Ultimately, work-from-home success depends on something we've largely forgotten how to do: monotask. More than any technique, this is a mindset: the understanding (backed by science) that <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2016/05/01/fashion/monotasking-drop-everything-and-read-this-story.html\">we get way more done</a> when we're doing one thing at a time. Working from home can actually nurture this kind of focus if you take control of your environment.&#160;</p><p>This also means setting clear boundaries for when work stops. Without the cues of the office, working hours have become more nebulous. During the pandemic's early weeks, <a href=\"https://hbswk.hbs.edu/item/you-re-right-you-are-working-longer-and-attending-more-meetings\">the average workday increased</a> by 8.2% worldwide. To keep my personal life separate from my work life, I think about how many hours a day I'm going to work and, when I meet them, I'm done. Communicate your working hours to your team and invite them to do the same for you. When your workday is over, turn your computer off — like all the way off, not just to sleep — to signal to yourself that you've clocked out.&#160;</p><h2><strong>Getting to know your team beyond the water cooler</strong></h2><p>Remote work has reinforced the fact that we're all individual people, not cogs in a machine, and<a href=\"https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fpsyg.2020.00963/full\"> we work better</a> when we're treated as such. As a leader, I've realized how counterintuitive it was to expect everyone to thrive in the<a href=\"https://www.thearticle.com/the-death-of-the-office\"> traditional office environment</a>. What's needed, more than anything, is choice.&#160;</p><p>This experience has actually transformed how I approach my team. Instead of fixating on getting back to the office, at my company we are doing what we can to help people thrive at home. For starters, we've allowed anyone to take any gear from the office that they want to use at home, and we're also moving away from blanket policies that treat everyone like they're the same. We're working to find ways to meet our organizational goals by being more respectful of people's singular needs. This means being open to different work schedules or hours for different people on the team.</p><p>For all the challenges of working from home, we have a golden opportunity to start to redefine work on our terms. How we set up our home office is a big part of that. Whether that means fancy gear, cool art, or extra soundproofing, the point is that the choice is yours. Take it.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/benjamin-crudo/\"><em>Ben Crudo</em></a><em> is CEO of </em><a href=\"https://www.diffagency.com/?utm_medium=pr&utm_source=csuite&utm_campaign=benpublicationsications\"><em>Diff Agency</em></a><em>. A retailer turned technologist, Ben is an ecommerce expert helping retailers win today and tomorrow.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f8445be642e9400180b54c2?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"61cb5ae4c49ebfeed7878d429a7f2851","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn93@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-58-234_6218e0fb2d8e05f9.webp","destWidth":709,"destHeight":532,"sourceBytes":23660,"destBytes":23660,"author":"mfox@businessinsider.com (Matthew Fox)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f8445acbab422001979abbe?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn76@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-55-671_e23bf82d49dc571f.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f844d0a642e9400180b54cb?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn52@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-56-161_c9546f7c26a4240b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-05-01-063_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=rmgtGGVVnrI:3FStwJw0tr8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn26@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-56-871_bba989877eda6e8b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=rmgtGGVVnrI:3FStwJw0tr8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn72@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-05-00-757_a42b4cc0212aa643.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn68@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-57-018_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=rmgtGGVVnrI:3FStwJw0tr8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn15@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-53-323_888b24916ab58da0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/rmgtGGVVnrI":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522289929},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:49","title":"A network of teen fact-checkers is tackling online misinformation ahead of the election — here's what they want you to know about spotting falsified facts","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/poynter-teen-fact-checkers-tackle-misinformation-ahead-of-election-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f778b1f282c500018c78660?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman standing alone with phone in city, people moving around her\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">d3sign/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A program from the Poynter Institute for Media Studies, the MediaWise Teen Fact-Checking Network, is training Gen Z middle- and high-schoolers to spot and debunk viral misinformation online.</li>\n<li>Misinformation, or false and inaccurate news portrayed as fact, has risen across social media platforms in the wake of the 2020 election, the coronavirus pandemic, and the nationwide protests.</li>\n<li>MediaWise's fact-checkers warn that anyone &#8212; regardless of age, political affiliation, or access to technology &#8212; can succumb to the kind of falsified information that spreads on platforms like Twitter, Facebook, and Instagram.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>From the 2020 election to the surging pandemic and nationwide protests, a perfect storm of conditions has caused <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/misinformation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">misinformation</a> to thrive online across social media platforms, at times <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/at-least-800-people-died-coronavirus-misinformation-3-months-2020-8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">leading to deadly consequences</a>. But, an army of teens is rising to combat misinformation. Trained through <a href=\"https://www.poynter.org/teen-fact-checking-network/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Poynter's MediaWise Teen Fact-Checking Network</a>, they have learned how to discern fact from fiction online.</p><p>The teen fact-checkers warn that misinformation typically provokes a strong emotional reaction from its consumers — and, combined with falsehood and inaccuracy, the false \"facts\" only serve to stoke long-held divisions and fuel political polarization. Often defined as digital natives, these Gen Z-ers view it as their responsibility to spread awareness about the dangers of believing what you read online.</p><p>Poynter's MediaWise Teen Fact-Checking Network, targeted toward middle- and high-schoolers, teaches Gen Z teens how to spot and debunk misinformation online. With the help of the Google News Initiative, the MediaWise program has trained over 100 teens since the program began in 2018. Together, they've produced more than 400 fact-checks in line with <a href=\"https://www.ifcncodeofprinciples.poynter.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">editorial standards from the International Fact-Checking Network</a>.</p><p>In July, MediaWise fact-checker Thea Barrett, 18, came across an infographic-style image that quoted US Education Secretary <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/betsy-devos\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Betsy DeVos</a> as saying that \"only 0.02%\" of K-12 children would die if they went back to school amid the coronavirus pandemic. The post's point: 0.02% still meant 14,740 children would die. When Barrett first saw the post on her feed, she immediately believed it. She didn't share it on Twitter, Instagram, or Facebook where it was rapidly spreading, but for days talked about it with friends and family.&#160;</p><p>Then she <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xY880KBDBnc\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fact-checked it for MediaWise</a>.</p><p>\"No part of it was true,\" she said. \"Every single part of it was false. And I just believed it because it spiked emotion in me, and it agreed with my reality, but I didn't even think about the fact that those numbers were made up. It was a false quote.\"</p><p>As Barrett and outlets such as <a href=\"https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/devos-only-student-deaths/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Snopes</a> and <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/factcheck/2020/07/14/fact-check-devos-never-said-only-0-02-kids-die-if-schools-open/5433134002/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USA Today</a> found, not only was the 14,740 number incorrect (0.02% of total US K-12 students would actually be about 11,000 children), but so was the entire statement attributed to DeVos. Despite there being no record of DeVos ever making that claim, the piece of misinformation went viral — it wasn't just shared by Gen Z-ers, but also by teachers, students, and concerned citizens across generations.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f778de2282c500018c7866d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"thea barret fact check\" height=\"953\" width=\"536\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>With the help of MediaWise, Thea Barrett created a YouTube tutorial fact-checking the viral claim attributed to Betsy DeVos.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Grace Eliza Goodwin/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>MediaWise's fact-checking program trains teens to look out for widely circulated claims like this one. According to Katy Byron, program manager at MediaWise, the three most common types of online misinformation come in the forms of manipulated videos and photos (including what's commonly referred to as \"cheap fakes\"), manipulated infographics, and screenshots of content from one platform that get cross-posted to another platform and manipulated along the way. The network encourages its fact-checkers to ask three critical questions when they encounter any information online, no matter how reputable the source may seem: who is behind the information, what is the evidence, and what do other sources say.&#160;</p><p>It's not just teens who believe false information shared online. According to a <a href=\"https://www.journalism.org/2016/12/15/many-americans-believe-fake-news-is-sowing-confusion/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">study conducted by Pew Research Center in 2016</a>, about a quarter of Americans say they have shared inaccurate or false news online, whether they were aware of it or not. In fact, a misconception about misinformation is that it's only an older generation that succumbs to inaccurate or out-of-context claims online.&#160;</p><p>But according to Byron, \"a lot of people assume that teenagers — because they're digitally savvy and grew up with the internet — are better at identifying misinformation. But that is not true.\" MediaWise believes that regardless of one's generation, upbringing, or level of access to technology, media literacy is something that must be taught.&#160;</p><p>According to Barrett, what was so effective about the false Betsy DeVos statement was that it sparked a strong emotional reaction in those who believed and shared it, and it confirmed their existing beliefs by providing facts and numbers — however untrue they turned out to be — about the danger of reopening schools. Barrett believes that because misinformation triggers emotion and stirs confirmation bias, it can fuel the deeply polarized divide between political parties, or anyone of opposing viewpoints.&#160;</p><p>\"Misinformation really does just start to seep into our communities, and so I think that plays a huge role in causing that divide to grow. Because if there's already a gap, and then you're putting false information out to grow that gap, and you're adding a lot of uncertainty or a lot of emotion into that,\" she said, \"of course that's going to make two parties separate even more.\"</p><p>For one of MediaWise's current teen fact-checkers, Bridgette Adu-Wadier, 17, misinformation feels exacerbated by a fast-paced news climate where consumers devour information without stopping to think critically.&#160;</p><p>\"Media literacy involves knowing how to fact-check information on your own, as well as being aware of how the media shapes public opinion, especially through bias,\" she said. \"I think a lot of people overlook how impactful headlines can be and how they can shape people's perceptions and prejudices, especially involving reports on police brutality, and how they describe people of color involved in those events.\"</p><p>Adu-Wadier views it as her responsibility, and everyone's, to take control of their news consumption by slowing down and fact-checking. A self-described history nerd, she believes that \"misinformation is so harmful because at a certain point, this present that we're living in is going to be in those history textbooks that students read. Facts are important because they fuel history as well as journalism. And facts help combat misinformation and biases that can keep people from understanding the bigger picture.\"</p><p>Barrett and Adu-Wadier have used their training to help others understand that just because something is portrayed as news online, doesn't mean it's true. Although it's one small corner of the internet they're shaping, they're hopeful that it will lead to lasting change.&#160;</p><p>\"We're not changing the world right here, but we are slowly making people more aware of the information they're putting out into the world. And that is how we stop the spread of misinformation,\" Barrett said. \"I believe that it's on all of us to be critical thinkers. And so, I am hopeful that one day we will be at a point where we don't have to stress about the amount of misinformation in our world.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Thayer/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Stocks could suffer in the near term if a Democrat \"blue wave\" in November brings a higher capital gains tax rate in 2022, but any impact would be brief, JPMorgan said on Friday.</strong></li><li><strong>If a higher rate comes into effect on January 1, 2022, there could be some downward pressure on equities in the fourth-quarter next said.</strong></li><li><strong>Under Biden's proposal, the maximum tax rate for long-term capital gains could rise to 39.6% from the current level of 23.8%&#160;</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>A Democratic sweep in the November elections would push the US capital gains tax rate up by 2022, but any impact on equities would be short-lived, according to JPMorgan.</p><p>Markets are increasingly pricing in a \"Blue Wave\" victory, one in which Joe Biden emerges as the presidential winner and the Democratic Party would be handed control of the Senate, as well as retaining control of Congress.</p><p>That would suggest an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-your-tax-rate-will-be-under-biden-tax-plan-2020-9?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">increase in taxes for wealthy Americans</a>, including capital gains.</p><p>If a higher rate on capital gains comes into effect on January 1, 2022, there would be some downward pressure on equity markets in the fourth-quarter of 2021, strategists led by Nikolaos Panigirtzoglou said in a noted dated October 9.</p><p>But once the new tax rate takes effect, stocks are likely to resume an upward trajectory, similar to the trend seen in the first halves of 1987 and 2013 after hikes on some capital gains, they said.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">:&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-companies-with-best-profit-growth-goldman-2020-10\" impact from a prospective capital gains tax rate increase on risk taking and investors' attitude toward equities as an asset class, given the current low yield and high equity risk premium environment,\" JPMorgan said.</p><p>Under Biden's proposal, the maximum tax rate for long-term capital gains could rise to 39.6%, from the current level of 23.8%&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/polling-suggests-trump-chances-of-defeating-biden-rapidly-dwindling-2020-10\">With polls suggesting</a> President Donald Trump's reelection prospects look bleak, Wall Street is pivoting to the implications of a Democratic sweep that could pave the way for the party to make big changes to policy.</p><p>JPMorgan predicts there could be tax-related equity selling equal to about $200 billion, due to the prospective increase in capital gains tax. That could knock about 5% off US stocks — similar to the level seen in 1986 and 2012.</p><p>\"But such pressure is likely to be temporary and once the new capital gains tax rate is introduced, the equity market would likely resume its uptrend in even stronger manner,\" the bank's strategists wrote.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">:&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-spac-etf-spak-benefits-risks-for-retail-investors-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-spac-etf-spak-benefits-risks-for-retail-investors-2020-10\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">SPACs have generated a $39 billion frenzy in the US this year.
